من الرهن ما لا يكون منعقداً أصلاً كالباطل من البيع والفاسد ما يكون منعقداً لكن بوصف الفساد والمقابل به يكون مالاً مضموناً، وفي كل موضع لم يكن الرهن مالاً ولم يكن المقابل به مضموناً لا ينعقد الرهن أصلاً وهو الباطل، وتعتبر قيمة الرهن يوم القبض ولم يذكر المؤلف أحكام غلبة الماء على المرهونة قال في المحيط أرض مرهونة غلب عليها الماء بمنزلة العبد إذا أبق لأنهار بما ينزل عنها الماء فتكون الأرض منتفعاً بها فلا يسقط الدين لاحتمال العود كالآبق. ولو عبداً حلال الدم أو سرق عند الراهن فقطع عند المرتهن فذاك من ضمان الراهن ولم رهن يذهب من الدين شيء وبقي مرتهناً بجميع الدين عند الإمام، وعندهما السرقة عيب ويقوم سارقاً وحلال الدم وغير سارق وغير حلال الدم فيسقط من الدين بمقدار قيمته حلال الدم والقطع ويكون رهناً بحصة قيمته كذلك، ولو وجب عليه حد القذف أو الزنا عند المرتهن أو دخله عيب فيسقط من الدين بقدره رهن ثوباً يساوي خمسة دراهم ومثال ذهب يساري عشرة بخمسة دراهم فهلك الذهب وليس الثوب حتى الخرق ضمن قيمة الثوب يحسب ماله ذلك درهم وثلثان لأنه ذهب بإذهاب الذهب ثلثا الدين وذلك ثلاثة دراهم وثلث درهم من الأرض قال لأن بإزاء الذهب ثلث الدين وبإزاء الثوب ثلثه ، فإذا ذهب الذهب واستهلك الثوب يذهب بإذهاب الثوب ثلث الدين ويضمن مثقال الذهب فيكون رهناً عنده بثلاثة دراهم وثلث . وذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى حكم هلاك العين المرهونة في يد المرتهن ولم يذكر حكم نقصانها في الخلاصة : إذا نقصت العين المرهونة في يد المرتهن إن كان النقصان في عينها سقط من ولم يتعرض لما إذا كان بالدين رهنان من جهتين مختلفتين قال قاضيخان : الدين بقدره ا هـ . رجل عليه دين لآخر وبه كفيل فأخذ الطالب من الكفيل رهناً ومن الأصيل رهناً وأحدهما الآخر وبكل واحد وفاء بالدين فهلك أحد الرهنين عند المرتهن قال زفر رحمه الله تعالى : بعد أيهما هلك بكل الدين. وقال الإمام أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : إذا هلك الرهن الثاني؛ فإن كان الراهن علم بالرهن الأول فإن الثاني يهلك بنصف الدين وإن لم يعلم بذلك يهلك بجميع الدين. وذكر في كتاب الرهن أن الثاني يهلك بنصف الدين ولم يذكر العلم والجهل وهو الصحيح لأن كل واحد منهما يطالب بجميع الدين فيجعل الرهن الثاني زيادة في الرهن الأول، فإن كانت قيمتهما سواء قسم الدين عليهما فالثاني إذا هلك يهلك بنصف الدين وقد قالوا : لو شرط إذا ضاع يكون مجاناً فالشرط باطل ويهلك بالدين ولم يتعرض لما إذا هلك
Chapter of Pledge. If the journey is three days, then the wage is half on the pledger and half on the pledgee, because the slave is half guaranteed by the debt and half a trust, so the wage is between them proportionally. Among these is treating illnesses and wounds, because that is divided between the guaranteed part and the trust part proportionally; what affects the guaranteed part is upon the pledgee, and what affects the trust part is upon the pledger. It would be better if he said: it is guaranteed by the lesser of the value of the guaranteed part and the debt, to include when the value of the pawned item is more than the debt originally. The invalid (bāṭil) of pledge is that which is not contracted at all, like the invalid of sale; the defective (fāsid) is that which is contracted but with a description of defectiveness, and its counterpart is guaranteed property. In every case where the pledge is not property and the counterpart is not guaranteed, the pledge does not contract at all—that is the invalid. The value of the pledge is considered on the day of possession. The author did not mention the rulings of water overwhelming the pawned item. It is said in al-Muḥīṭ: A mortgaged land that is overcome by water is like a slave who has run away, because the water may recede from it, so the land can be benefited from; thus the debt is not dropped due to the possibility of its return, like the runaway. If the slave is of permissible blood (ḥalāl al-dam) or stolen at the pledger's, then cut at the pledgee's, that is from the pledger's guarantee, and nothing goes from the debt, and he remains a pledgee for the entire debt according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), theft is a defect, and it is valued as a thief and of permissible blood, and as non-thief and non-permissible blood; thus an amount equal to its value when of permissible blood and the cut is deducted from the debt, and it becomes a pledge for the share of its value likewise. If the ḥadd penalty for slander or adultery is due upon him at the pledgee's, or a defect enters it, then an amount equal to it is deducted from the debt. A man pawned a cloth worth five dirhams and as an example gold with ten dirhams' silver for five dirhams; the gold perished, and the cloth was not even a rag; he guarantees the value of the cloth, calculating that he has one and two-thirds dirhams, because the gold's removal took two-thirds of the debt, which is three and one-third dirhams from the land. He said: because against the gold is one-third of the debt, and against the cloth is one-third; so if the gold perishes and the cloth is consumed, the removal of the cloth takes one-third of the debt, and he guarantees the mithqāl of the gold, so it becomes a pledge with him for three and one-third dirhams. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned the ruling of the destruction of the pawned item in the hands of the pledgee, but did not mention the ruling of its deficiency. In al-Khulāṣa: If the pawned item decreases in the hands of the pledgee, if the decrease is in its substance, something is deducted from the debt. He did not address when there are two pawns for the same debt from different parties. Qāḍīkhān said: the debt is proportional. A man owes a debt to another and has a surety (kafīl); the claimant took one pawn from the surety and one from the principal debtor, both equal, and each covers the debt. One of the two pawns perishes with the pledgee. Zufar said: whichever perishes, it perishes with the entire debt. Imam Abu Yusuf said: if the second pawn perishes, if the pledger knew of the first pawn, then the second perishes with half the debt; if he did not know, it perishes with the entire debt. It is mentioned in Kitāb al-Rahn that the second perishes with half the debt, and it did not mention knowledge and ignorance, and that is correct, because each of them is demanded for the entire debt, so the second pawn is considered an increase over the first. If their values are equal, the debt is divided between them; so if the second perishes, it perishes with half the debt. They said: if he stipulates that if it is lost it is gratis, the condition is void, and it perishes with the debt. And he did not address what if it perishes.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq covering multiple rulings on pledge (rahn). The text first discusses the expenses for returning a runaway slave: if the journey is three days, the wage is split equally between pledger and pledgee because the slave is partly guaranteed (for the debt) and partly a trust. Medical treatment is also divided proportionally. The author suggests a more precise definition: the pledge is guaranteed up to the lesser of the value of the guaranteed portion and the debt. Then the distinction between bāṭil (void) and fāsid (defective) pledge is clarified: bāṭil is not contracted at all, like a void sale; fāsid is contracted but with a defect, and the counterpart is guaranteed property. The value of the pledge is reckoned at the time of possession. The ruling on land overtaken by water is analogous to a runaway slave—the debt is not dropped because the water may recede. Next, a scenario where a slave with permissible blood (ḥalāl al-dam) or stolen is cut—according to Abu Hanifa, the pledgee remains entitled to the full debt; according to the two disciples, the theft is a defect, and the pledgee's claim is reduced proportionally. Similarly, if a ḥadd penalty becomes due, the debt is reduced. A numerical example illustrates how the loss is computed when multiple items are pawned. The passage then addresses a case with two pawns from different parties (the surety and the principal debtor). Zufar holds that whichever pawn perishes covers the entire debt; Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on the pledger's knowledge; the relied-upon ruling (ṣaḥīḥ) is that the second pawn perishes with half the debt if values are equal, treating it as an increase. Finally, a stipulation that loss is gratis is void, and the pawn still covers the debt.

Key Terms
غلبة الماء (ghalabat al-mā): Water overwhelming; temporary flooding of pawned land.
أبق (abaqa): Runaway (slave); used as analogy for temporary loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the flood on pawned land not a reason to drop the debt?
A) Because the land is still owned by the pledger
B) Because the water may recede and the land become useful again
C) Because the creditor must wait for the water to recede
D) Because the debt is guaranteed by other means

Key Takeaway
Temporary loss of benefit from a pawn does not discharge the debt if there is hope of restoration.

Defect in Pawn: Reduction of Debt and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on debt reduction due to defects in pawn, with numerical example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether a defect (e.g., theft, ḥalāl al-dam, ḥadd) in a pawn reduces the debt, and apply the numerical example for partial loss.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: full debt remains; Abu Yusuf & Muhammad: debt reduced by value of defect; the latter is often relied upon.

The passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding defects in a pawn that occur while in the pledgee's possession. The scenarios include a slave of permissible blood (ḥalāl al-dam) who is cut, theft, and ḥadd penalties. The text also provides a numerical example of partial loss involving a cloth and gold to illustrate proportional reduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defect scenario
A pawned slave of permissible blood (ḥalāl al-dam) or a thief is cut while in the pledgee's possession. Also, if a ḥadd penalty (e.g., slander or adultery) becomes due, or any defect enters the item.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the debt remains intact; no reduction occurs because the defect is considered from the pledger's guarantee.
The text: 'fadhālika min ḍamān al-rāhin'.
3
State the position of the two disciples (Ṣāḥibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider theft and similar defects as reducing the value; the debt is decreased proportionally to the lost value.
They value the slave as a thief vs. non-thief, and deduct the difference.
4
Apply to ḥadd and other defects
Similarly, if a ḥadd penalty is incurred or any defect occurs, the debt is reduced by the amount of the diminution in value.
5
Work through the numerical example
A man pawns a cloth worth 5 dirhams and gold worth 10 dirhams' silver for a debt of 5 dirhams. The gold perishes. The cloth is lost (or not). The calculation shows how the debt is divided proportionally between the items.
The gold's removal takes 2/3 of the debt, cloth takes 1/3.

Source Text

الأمانة بالحصص وما أصاب المضمون فعلى المرتهن، وأما أصاب الأمانة فعلى الراهن. ولو قال وهو مضمون بالأقل من قيمة المضمون ومن الدين لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان قيمة المرهون أكثر من الدين في الأصل والباطل Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq covering multiple rulings on pledge (rahn). The text first discusses the expenses for returning a runaway slave: if the journey is three days, the wage is split equally between pledger and pledgee because the slave is partly guaranteed (for the debt) and partly a trust. Key Terms
حلال الدم (ḥalāl al-dam): A slave whose blood is permissible to shed (e.g., convicted of a capital crime).
حد القذف (ḥadd al-qadhf): The fixed penalty for false accusation of adultery.

A) The debt is reduced by the slave's value

D) The debt is halved

Two Pawns from Different Parties: Dispute and Relied-Upon Ruling
Dispute on loss of one of two pawns from different parties, with relied-upon ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on the loss of one of two pawns from different parties (surety and principal) and state the relied-upon ruling that the second perishes with half the debt.

Core Idea
When two equal-value pawns from surety and principal secure the same debt, the second pawn's loss discharges half the debt.

This passage addresses a scenario where a creditor holds two pawns from two different persons: the principal debtor and a surety (kafīl). The debt is owed by the principal. If one of the pawns perishes, how much of the debt is discharged? The text records the opinions of Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and the relied-upon view from Kitāb al-Rahn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person owes a debt and has a surety. The creditor takes a pawn from the surety and one from the principal debtor. Both pawns are of equal value and each individually covers the debt. One of them perishes.
2
State Zufar's position
Zufar holds that whichever pawn perishes, it discharges the entire debt. He treats each pawn as independent security.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf differentiates: if the second pawn (from principal) perishes and the pledger (principal) knew of the first pawn, then the second perishes with half the debt; if he did not know, it perishes with the entire debt.
Knowledge affects the treatment.
4
State the relied-upon view (from Kitāb al-Rahn)
The text says the second pawn perishes with half the debt, without regard to knowledge. This is considered correct (wa huwa al-ṣaḥīḥ).
The reasoning: each party is liable for the entire debt, so the second pawn is an increase; thus the debt is divided proportionally.
5
Consider the stipulation condition
If the parties stipulate that if the pawn is lost it is gratis (i.e., no liability), the condition is void and the pawn still covers the debt.

Source Text

كتاب الرهن مسيرة ثلاثة أيام فإن الجعل على الراهن وعلى المرتهن نصفان لأن العبد نصفه مضمون بالدين ونصفه أمانة فيكون الجعل بينهما بالحصص. ومنها مداواة الأمراض والجروح لأنه ينقسم ذلك على المضمون وعلى الأمانة بالحصص وما أصاب المضمون فعلى المرتهن، وأما أصاب الأمانة فعلى الراهن. ولو قال وهو مضمون بالأقل من قيمة المضمون ومن الدين لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان قيمة المرهون أكثر من الدين في الأصل والباطل من الرهن ما لا يكون منعقداً أصلاً كالباطل من البيع والفاسد ما يكون منعقداً لكن بوصف الفساد والمقابل به يكون مالاً مضموناً، وفي كل موضع لم يكن الرهن مالاً ولم يكن المقابل به مضموناً لا ينعقد الرهن الأرض قال لأن بإزاء الذهب ثلث الدين وبإزاء الثوب ثلثه ، فإذا ذهب الذهب واستهلك الثوب يذهب بإذهاب الثوب ثلث الدين ويضمن مثقال الذهب فيكون رهناً عنده بثلاثة دراهم وثلث . وذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى حكم قاضيخان : الدين بقدره ا هـ . رجل عليه دين لآخر وبه كفيل فأخذ الطالب من الكفيل رهناً ومن الأصيل رهناً وأحدهما الآخر وبكل واحد وفاء بالدين فهلك أحد الرهنين عند المرتهن قال زفر رحمه الله تعالى : بعد أيهما هلك بكل الدين. وقال الإمام أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : إذا هلك الرهن الثاني؛ فإن كان الراهن علم بالرهن الأول فإن الثاني يهلك بنصف الدين وإن لم يعلم بذلك يهلك بجميع الدين. وذكر في كتاب الرهن أن الدين وقد قالوا : لو شرط إذا ضاع يكون مجاناً فالشرط باطل ويهلك بالدين ولم يتعرض لما إذا هلك
Chapter of Pledge. If the journey is three days, then the wage is half on the pledger and half on the pledgee, because the slave is half guaranteed by the debt and half a trust, so the wage is between them proportionally. Among these is treating illnesses and wounds, because that is divided between the guaranteed part and the trust part proportionally; what affects the guaranteed part is upon the pledgee, and what affects the trust part is upon the pledger. It would be better if he said: it is guaranteed by the lesser of the value of the guaranteed part and the debt, to include when the value of the pawned item is more than the debt originally. The invalid (bāṭil) of pledge is that which is not contracted at all, like the invalid of sale; the defective (fāsid) is that which is contracted but with a description of defectiveness, and its counterpart is guaranteed property. In every case where the pledge is not property and the counterpart is not guaranteed, the pledge does not contract at all—that is the invalid. The value of the pledge is considered on the day of possession. The author did not mention the rulings of water overwhelming the pawned item. It is said in al-Muḥīṭ: A mortgaged land that is overcome by water is like a slave who has run away, because the water may recede from it, so the land can be benefited from; thus the debt is not dropped due to the possibility of its return, like the runaway. If the slave is of permissible blood (ḥalāl al-dam) or stolen at the pledger's, then cut at the pledgee's, that is from the pledger's guarantee, and nothing goes from the debt, and he remains a pledgee for the entire debt according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), theft is a defect, and it is valued as a thief and of permissible blood, and as non-thief and non-permissible blood; thus an amount equal to its value when of permissible blood and the cut is deducted from the debt, and it becomes a pledge for the share of its value likewise. If the ḥadd penalty for slander or adultery is due upon him at the pledgee's, or a defect enters it, then an amount equal to it is deducted from the debt. A man pawned a cloth worth five dirhams and as an example gold with ten dirhams' silver for five dirhams; the gold perished, and the cloth was not even a rag; he guarantees the value of the cloth, calculating that he has one and two-thirds dirhams, because the gold's removal took two-thirds of the debt, which is three and one-third dirhams from the land. He said: because against the gold is one-third of the debt, and against the cloth is one-third; so if the gold perishes and the cloth is consumed, the removal of the cloth takes one-third of the debt, and he guarantees the mithqāl of the gold, so it becomes a pledge with him for three and one-third dirhams. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned the ruling of the destruction of the pawned item in the hands of the pledgee, but did not mention the ruling of its deficiency. In al-Khulāṣa: If the pawned item decreases in the hands of the pledgee, if the decrease is in its substance, something is deducted from the debt. He did not address when there are two pawns for the same debt from different parties. Qāḍīkhān said: the debt is proportional. A man owes a debt to another and has a surety (kafīl); the claimant took one pawn from the surety and one from the principal debtor, both equal, and each covers the debt. One of the two pawns perishes with the pledgee. Zufar said: whichever perishes, it perishes with the entire debt. Imam Abu Yusuf said: if the second pawn perishes, if the pledger knew of the first pawn, then the second perishes with half the debt; if he did not know, it perishes with the entire debt. It is mentioned in Kitāb al-Rahn that the second perishes with half the debt, and it did not mention knowledge and ignorance, and that is correct, because each of them is demanded for the entire debt, so the second pawn is considered an increase over the first. If their values are equal, the debt is divided between them; so if the second perishes, it perishes with half the debt. They said: if he stipulates that if it is lost it is gratis, the condition is void, and it perishes with the debt. And he did not address what if it perishes.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq covering multiple rulings on pledge (rahn). The text first discusses the expenses for returning a runaway slave: if the journey is three days, the wage is split equally between pledger and pledgee because the slave is partly guaranteed (for the debt) and partly a trust. Medical treatment is also divided proportionally. The author suggests a more precise definition: the pledge is guaranteed up to the lesser of the value of the guaranteed portion and the debt. Then the distinction between bāṭil (void) and fāsid (defective) pledge is clarified: bāṭil is not contracted at all, like a void sale; fāsid is contracted but with a defect, and the counterpart is guaranteed property. The value of the pledge is reckoned at the time of possession. The ruling on land overtaken by water is analogous to a runaway slave—the debt is not dropped because the water may recede. Next, a scenario where a slave with permissible blood (ḥalāl al-dam) or stolen is cut—according to Abu Hanifa, the pledgee remains entitled to the full debt; according to the two disciples, the theft is a defect, and the pledgee's claim is reduced proportionally. Similarly, if a ḥadd penalty becomes due, the debt is reduced. A numerical example illustrates how the loss is computed when multiple items are pawned. The passage then addresses a case with two pawns from different parties (the surety and the principal debtor). Zufar holds that whichever pawn perishes covers the entire debt; Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on the pledger's knowledge; the relied-upon ruling (ṣaḥīḥ) is that the second pawn perishes with half the debt if values are equal, treating it as an increase. Finally, a stipulation that loss is gratis is void, and the pawn still covers the debt.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafīl): Surety; one who guarantees the debt of another.
أصيل (aṣīl): Principal debtor; the person primarily liable for the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in Kitāb al-Rahn, if a creditor holds two equal-value pawns from the surety and principal and the second pawn (from principal) perishes, how much of the debt is discharged?
A) The entire debt
B) Half the debt
C) One-third of the debt
D) No debt is discharged

Key Takeaway
When two pawns from different parties secure the same debt, the loss of the second pawn discharges half the debt if values are equal.

Forgiveness of Debt and Pledge Liability: Qiyās vs Istiḥsān
Ruling on pledgee liability after forgiveness of debt with qiyās/istiḥsān reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on pledgee liability after forgiving the debt, and distinguish the qiyās and istiḥsān reasoning.

Core Idea
Forgive the debt, the pawn becomes a trust; destroy it after, you are not liable—istiḥsān overrides qiyās.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi debate: if a pledgee forgives the debt (hiba/ibra) and the pawn subsequently perishes without the pledgee's fault, is he liable? The strict analogy (qiyās) says yes, but juristic preference (istiḥsān) says no. We will walk through the reasoning of both sides and identify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is forgiveness of debt (hiba/ibra) followed by destruction of the pawn. The disputed ruling is whether the pledgee is liable.
2
Understand the qiyās argument
Follow the analogy: the pawn is guaranteed by possession; destruction marks satisfaction; forgiveness after satisfaction does not remove liability. This is Zufar's view.
3
Understand the istiḥsān argument
The guarantee depends on the debt's existence; once the debt falls away, the purpose of the pledge is gone, so the pawn becomes a trust. This is the view of the three imams.
4
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The relied-upon position is istiḥsān because it is the view of the majority and supported by the principle that the guarantee is conditional.
5
Distinguish from satisfaction
Note that if the pawn is destroyed after the pledgee has already received payment, the liability is different: he must return what he took. This is not forgiveness but actual satisfaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان أقل صار مستوفياً بقدر دينه ويرجع المرتهن وبالفضل وهب المرتهن الدين من الراهن أو أبرأه عنه فهلك الرهن عنده من غير منع يضمن المرتهن وله أن يطالب في يد المرتهن بعد أن أبرأه الراهن أو وهبه الدين أو فصول : أحدها في هلاك الرهن قبل الإبراء، والثاني في هلاكه بعد الاستيفاء، والثالث في هلاكه بعد فسخ الرهن وإقالته، والرابع في استحساناً هلاكه بعد استعماله . قال رحمه الله : ( وهب المرتهن الدين من الراهن أو أبرأه عنه فهلك الرهن عنده من غير منع يضمن (المرتهن قياساً وهو قول زفر ولا يضمن استحساناً، ولو منعه حتى هلك ووجه القياس أن الرهن صار مضموناً على المرتهن بالقبض واليد لأن به يصير ضمن قيمته اتفاقاً مستوفاً للدين ويده على الرهن يد استيفاء للدين ويتقرر ذلك بالهلاك وصار كأنه استوفى ثم أبرأه فيبقى مضموناً عليه لبقاء اليد والقبض فكذا هذا وجه الاستحسان أن الضمان قد ارتفع قبل تقرر حكمه ووجوبه لأن ضمان الرهن إنما يجب إما بحقيقة الرهن أو بجهته وقد ارتفع العقد والجهة بسقوط الدين فانتفى الضمان وذلك لأن قيام الدين ودوامه بشرط بقاء الرهن لأن الرهن شرع توثيقاً وتوكيداً للدين وبعد سقوطه لا يتصور توثيقه وتوكيد فلا فائدة في بقاء الرهن فلا يبقى فانحل الضمان لارتفاع مناطه فبقيت العين أمانة في يده بخلاف الاستيفاء لأن الاستيفاء يتقرر بالدين ولا يسقط أصلاً، ولهذا صحت الهبة والإبراء بعد الاستيفاء حتى يلزمه رد ما استوفاه ولا تصح الهبة والإبراء بعد هبة الدين وإبرائه. ولو أخذت المرأة رهناً بصداقها ثم طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها ثم هلك الرهن هلك بنصف الصداق لأن الصداق قد سقط فصار كالبراءة عن الدين ولو قبض المرتهن حقه ثم هلك الرهن عنده ولم يمنعه من قبضه وقيمته مثل الدين رد ما قبض لأن الدين لم يسقط لاستيفاء من وجه في حق بعض الأحكام وإن سقط في حق المطالبة لما بينا فصار مستوفياً ما قبض. بعدما استوفاه مرة If it was less, he becomes satisfied to the extent of his debt, and the pledgee gets back the surplus. If the pledgee gives the debt as a gift (hiba) to the pledger or releases him (ibra) from it, and then the pawn perishes with him without prevention, the pledgee is liable; and he has the right to demand [something] in his hand after the pledger released him or gave him the debt or transferred it. It is said in al-Khulāṣa: If he released him from the debt, or transferred it to him, or gave it to him as a gift while the slave was in the hand of the pledgee, and it perished in his hand without him preventing it, he is not liable—this is the statement of our three companions (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad)—unlike if the pledger released him regarding what remained of the debt, then the pawn perished in the hands of the pledgee, he must return what he received. Even if they both agree that no debt remains guaranteed. If the pledgee transferred (hawala) the pledger with the pawn to a person who has the pawn, then the pawned slave dies before he returns it, then the transfer is void. In al-Mabsūṭ, its issues are divided into sections: one on the destruction of the pawn before release, second on its destruction after satisfaction, third on its destruction after rescission and cancellation of the pledge, fourth on its destruction after use—by istiḥsān. He said: 'If the pledgee gives the debt as a gift to the pledger or releases him from it, and then the pawn perishes with him without prevention, the pledgee is liable by qiyās—this is the statement of Zufar—and he is not liable by istiḥsān. Even if he prevented him until it perished. The basis of qiyās is that the pawn becomes guaranteed upon the pledgee by possession and hand, because by it he becomes guaranteed for its value by agreement, satisfied for the debt; his hand over the pawn is a hand of satisfaction for the debt, and that is established by destruction; it is as if he satisfied then released him, so it remains guaranteed upon him due to the continuation of hand and possession. Likewise, this is the basis of istiḥsān: that the guarantee has been removed before its ruling and obligation are settled, because the guarantee of the pawn is established either by the essence of the pledge or by its cause; the contract and cause have been removed by the falling away of the debt, so the guarantee is negated. That is because the establishment and continuance of the debt are conditional upon the survival of the pawn, for the pawn is legislated as a confirmation and reinforcement for the debt; after its falling away, its confirmation and reinforcement cannot be imagined, so there is no benefit in the survival of the pawn, so it does not remain; thus the guarantee is dissolved due to the removal of its basis, so the item remains a trust in his hand—unlike satisfaction, because satisfaction is established by the debt and does not fall away entirely. Hence, gift and release are valid after satisfaction, so he must return what he took, but gift and release after gift and release of the debt are not valid. If a woman takes a pawn for her dower, then her husband divorces her before consummation, then the pawn perishes, it perishes with half the dower because the dower has fallen away, so it becomes like release from the debt. If the pledgee took his right, then the pawn perished with him and he did not prevent him from taking it, and its value is like the debt, he returns what he took because the debt has not fallen away due to satisfaction from one aspect with regard to some rulings, although it has fallen away in terms of demand, as we explained, so he becomes satisfied for what he took, after having satisfied once by the destruction, so he must return what he took later. If the debt was a loan of food, and the one upon whom it was due bought it with dirhams and gave them to the pledgee, then the pawn perished, the pledgee must return the like of that food. This issue clarifies that the pledgee becomes satisfied at the time of destruction, not at the time of possession, because if he became satisfied at the time of possession, the sale would not be permissible since there would be nothing in the debtor's liability. A third party voluntarily paid the debt of the pledgee, then the pawn perished in the hand of the pledgee, he must return the money to the volunteer because he satisfied the debt from
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq discusses the effect of forgiveness (hiba/ibra) of the debt on the liability of the pledge (rahn). It begins with a scenario: if the pawn is less than the debt, the pledgee becomes satisfied to that extent and must return any surplus. Then the core ruling: if the pledgee gives the debt as a gift or releases the pledger, and then the pawn perishes without the pledgee preventing it, there is a disagreement. By qiyās (analogy), the pledgee remains liable because the pawn is guaranteed by possession; this is Zufar's view. By istiḥsān (juristic preference), the pledgee is not liable because the guarantee is lifted once the debt is gone—the purpose of the pledge is security for the debt, and without debt, the pawn becomes a trust. The relied-upon view (muftā bihi) is istiḥsān, as it is the position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The text distinguishes this from satisfaction (istiʾfāʾ) after receiving payment: if the pledgee had already taken his right (i.e., the debt was paid), then the pawn perishes, he must return what he took because the destruction establishes that he had already satisfied in effect. Other cases include: a woman's pawn for dower—if divorce before consummation halves the dower, the pawn perishes with half; if the pledgee receives payment then the pawn perishes, he returns the payment; if a third party pays the debt voluntarily, then the pawn perishes, he returns the money to the volunteer because the pledgee is deemed to have satisfied from the volunteer's payment. The passage also clarifies that satisfaction occurs at the time of destruction, not at the time of possession, to avoid inconsistency with sales.

Key Terms
هبة (hiba): A gift of the debt by the pledgee to the pledger, resulting in forgiveness of the debt.
إبراء (ibra): A release or discharge from the debt granted by the pledgee to the pledger.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning that compares the case of forgiveness followed by destruction to the case of satisfaction (istiʾfāʾ) by destruction.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that sets aside the strict analogy (qiyās) in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a pledgee forgives the debt and then the pawn perishes without the pledgee's fault, is the pledgee liable?
A) Yes, because the pawn was in his possession.
B) No, because the debt no longer exists and the pawn becomes a trust.
C) Yes, because forgiveness does not change the guarantee.
D) No, but only if the pawn perishes by an act of God.

Key Takeaway
When the debt is forgiven before the pawn perishes, the guarantee dissolves and the pawn becomes a trust; the pledgee is not liable by istiḥsān.

Pawn Perishing After Debt Forgiveness: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability after debt forgiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi istihsan ruling on mortgagee's liability when the pawn perishes after debt forgiveness and evaluate Zufar's qiyas counter-argument.

Core Idea
When the debt is extinguished, the guarantee dissolves; the pawn becomes a trust.

This passage presents a classic intra-madhhab dispute where Zufar follows qiyas (analogy) to hold the mortgagee liable, while the majority of Hanafi imams adopt istihsan (juristic preference) to absolve him. The core question is: does the mortgagee's possession remain a 'hand of guarantee' after the debt is forgiven? The answer determines whether he must compensate the mortgagor for the perished pawn. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh qiyas against istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the exact scenario: mortgagee forgives the debt, then pawn perishes. Identify the two positions: Zufar (liable by qiyas) and majority (not liable by istihsan).
The dispute is about daman (liability), not the validity of the forgiveness.
2
Analyze Zufar's qiyas
Trace the analogy: the pawn is considered as if the mortgagee already received his debt. When he later forgives, the guarantee remains because receipt of debt is irreversible. The 'hand as receipt' continues.
Qiyas compares to the case where the mortgagee actually receives the debt then afterwards forgives.
3
Understand the istihsan rationale
Istihsan looks at the purpose of the pawn (tawthiq – security). Since the debt is extinguished, the basis for guarantee is removed. The pawn then becomes a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hand.
The rationale is that without a debt, there can be no security; the pawn's purpose is gone.
4
Contrast with actual receipt
Note the distinction: if the mortgagee had received his debt (e.g., the pawn was sold and proceeds taken) and then later forgave, the guarantee persists. But here forgiveness happens before any receipt, so the debt never was satisfied.
This distinction is key to the istihsan reasoning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is the relied-upon position: no liability. Zufar's view is marjuh (weak/preferred against).
The author clearly states that istihsan is the correct view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهب المرتهن الدين من الراهن أو أبرأه عنه فهلك الرهن عنده من غير منع يضمن المرتهن قياساً وهو قول زفر ولا يضمن استحساناً، ولو منعه حتى هلك ووجه القياس أن الرهن صار مضموناً على المرتهن بالقبض واليد لأن به يصير ضمان قيمته اتفاقاً مستوفاً للدين ويده على الرهن يد استيفاء للدين ويتقرر ذلك بالهلاك وصار كأنه استوفى ثم أبرأه فيبقى مضموناً عليه لبقاء اليد والقبض فكذا هذا وجه الاستحسان أن الضمان قد ارتفع قبل تقرر حكمه ووجوبه لأن ضمان الرهن إنما يجب إما بحقيقة الرهن أو بجهته وقد ارتفع العقد والجهة بسقوط الدين فانتفى الضمان وذلك لأن قيام الدين ودوامه بشرط بقاء الرهن لأن الرهن شرع توثيقاً وتوكيداً للدين وبعد سقوطه لا يتصور توثيقه وتوكيد فلا فائدة في بقاء الرهن فلا يبقى فانحل الضمان لارتفاع مناطه فبقيت العين أمانة في يده بخلاف الاستيفاء لأن الاستيفاء يتقرر بالدين ولا يسقط أصلاً، ولهذا صحت الهبة والإبراء بعد الاستيفاء حتى يلزمه رد ما استوفاه ولا تصح الهبة والإبراء بعد هبة الدين وإبرائه.
If the mortgagee gives the debt as a gift to the mortgagor or discharges him from it, and then the pawn perishes in his possession without any prevention, the mortgagee is liable by qiyas, and that is the view of Zufar, and he is not liable by istihsan. And if he prevented him until it perished... The basis of qiyas is that the pawn became guaranteed upon the mortgagee by taking possession and custody, because by that he becomes, by agreement, a recipient of the debt through its value, and his hand on the pawn is a hand of receipt of the debt, and that becomes established by destruction, and it is as if he had received (the debt) and then discharged him, so it remains guaranteed upon him due to the continuation of possession and custody. Similarly here. The basis of istihsan is that the guarantee had been removed before its ruling and obligation were established, because the guarantee of the pawn is obligated either by the reality of the pawn or by its aspect, and both the contract and the aspect have been removed by the falling away of the debt, so the guarantee is negated. That is because the existence and continuation of the debt is conditional upon the continuation of the pawn, because the pawn is prescribed as a security and reinforcement for the debt; after its fall, its securing and reinforcing cannot be imagined, so there is no benefit in the continuation of the pawn, so it does not remain, and the guarantee is dissolved because its basis is removed, and the object remains as a trust in his hand, unlike receipt (of the debt) because receipt is established by the debt and does not fall at all; therefore gift and discharge after receipt are valid, such that he is obliged to return what he received, and gift and discharge after gift of the debt and its discharge are not valid.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage presents a core intra-madhhab dispute concerning the liability of a mortgagee (creditor) when the pawned item perishes in his possession after he has voluntarily forgiven the debt or gifted it to the mortgagor (debtor). The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute between the view of Zufar (who follows qiyas) and the position of the majority of Hanafi imams (who adopt istihsan). The author first states the matn ruling: in this scenario, the mortgagee would be liable by analogical reasoning (qiyas) but not liable by juristic preference (istihsan). He then explains the basis of each. Qiyas analogizes this situation to the case where the mortgagee actually receives his debt and then the pawn perishes: in that case, the mortgagee is liable because the pawn is considered as having been received in satisfaction of the debt, and the subsequent discharge does not remove the liability since the debt was already effectively satisfied. Similarly, by qiyas, forgiving the debt after the pawn is in his possession is like receiving the debt first and then forgiving it, so the guarantee remains. Istihsan, however, looks at the underlying rationale: the guarantee (daman) of the pawn is contingent upon the existence and continuation of the debt itself. Since the debt has been completely extinguished by the gift or discharge, there is no purpose left for the pawn; it no longer serves as security. The contract of mortgage and its purpose have ended, so the pawn reverts to being a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hand, and he is not liable for its destruction unless he was negligent. This is contrasted with the case of actual receipt of the debt: if the mortgagee received his due and then the pawn perished, the debt is considered satisfied from the moment of receipt, and subsequent discharge does not undo the fact that the debt was already paid – thus the guarantee persists.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability/guarantee: in this context, the obligation of the mortgagee to compensate for the value of the pawn if it perishes under his responsibility.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: a method of reasoning where the jurist prefers an alternative ruling over the one indicated by qiyas due to a stronger reason (e.g., necessity, custom, or underlying rationale).
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; the act of acquiring physical control over an object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgagee gives the debt as a gift to the mortgagor and then the pawn perishes in the mortgagee's hand without his fault, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The mortgagee is liable by qiyas, following Zufar.
B) The mortgagee is not liable by istihsan, which is the preferred view.
C) The mortgagee is always liable regardless of circumstances.
D) The mortgagee must return the debt to the mortgagor.

Key Takeaway
When a debt is forgiven, the pawn's guarantee dissolves and it becomes a trust – the mortgagee is not liable for accidental destruction.

Dower Pawn After Divorce Before Consummation
One of several sub-rulings on pawn destruction after debt discharge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a dower pawn perishes after a pre-consummation divorce and explain the legal analogy to discharge.

Core Idea
A pawn taken for dower that perishes after the dower is halved is treated as if the debt was discharged, so it perishes for half.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case from Hanafi fiqh: a woman takes a pawn for her full dower, but the husband divorces her before consummation, reducing the dower to half. If the pawn perishes after the divorce, what is the liability? The passage provides a ruling based on analogy to discharge (bara'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the debt
The pawn is taken by the wife for her dower (sadaq). After divorce before consummation, the dower is reduced by half.
The dower becomes half of the agreed amount.
2
Determine the effect of the divorce on the debt
The divorce causes the dower to fall to half, effectively discharging half of the debt.
This is similar to a partial discharge (ibra').
3
Apply the ruling on pawn destruction
Since the debt is discharged (half), the pawn is considered to have perished for that discharged portion. The wife loses half the pawn's value, but the husband is not liable for the other half.
The ruling uses the principle that destruction of a pawn after debt discharge is attributed to the discharged debt.
4
Understand the analogy to bara'ah
The text says 'like a discharge from the debt' because the divorce effectively forgives half the dower, so the pawn's destruction is treated as if it occurred after discharge.
This shows the Hanafi approach of treating legal events as analogous to explicit discharges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أخذت المرأة رهناً بصداقها ثم طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها ثم هلك الرهن هلك بنصف الصداق لأن الصداق قد سقط فصار كالبراءة عن الدين. ولو قبض المرتهن حقه ثم هلك الرهن عنده ولم يمنعه من قبضه وقيمته مثل الدين رد ما قبض لأن الدين لم يسقط لاستيفاء من وجه في حق بعض الأحكام وإن سقط في حق المطالبة لما بينا فصار مستوفياً ما قبض. بعدما استوفاه مرة حكماً بالهلاك فيلزمه رد ما قبض آخراً. ولو كان الدين طعاماً قرضاً فاشتراه من هو عليه بدراهم ودفعها إلى المرتهن ثم هلك الرهن فعلى المرتهن رد مثل ذلك الطعام وتبين بهذه المسألة أن المرتهن يصير مستوفياً وقت الهلاك دون القبض لأنه لو صار مستوفياً من وقت القبض لما جاز البيع لأنه ليس في ذمة الراهن شيء. قضى أجنبي دين المرتهن تطوعاً ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن رد يرد المال على المتطوع لأنه استوفى الدين من الراهن بالهلاك بعدما استوفاه من المتطوع فيجب عليه ذلك كما إذا استوفاه من الغريم ثم هلك الرهن. تصادق الراهن والمرتهن أن لا دين بعد أن اتفقا أنه ألف وهلك الرهن فعلى المرتهن أن يرد الألف لأن الرهن حين هلك كان مضموناً بالدين لأنهما لم يتصادقا أن لا قبل الهلاك فصار المرتهن مستوفياً للدين حكماً بالهلاك فصار كما لو استوفاه حقيقة، ولو تصادقا أن لا دين قبل الهلاك اختلف المشايخ فيه قيل يملك أمانة لأن الرهن حصل بدين مضمون يتوهم وجوبه فصار الرهن مضموناً بدين مظنون، فإذا زال التوهم بالتصادق على أن لا دين يزول الضمان كما لو زال بالإبراء والهبة وقيل يضمن لأنه توهم وجوب الدين لم يزل تصادقهما على أن لا دين لأن تصادقهما على عدم الدين لا يمنعهما عن التصادق على الوجوب بعد ذلك لجواز أن يتذكرا بعد ما تصادقا أنه كان عليه دين وإن بقي توهم الوجوب بقي مضموناً عليه لأن ما به يثبت الضمان وهو توهم الاقتراض منه في الثاني بامتناعه الاقتراض لم يزل الجواز أن يكون أقرضه بعد ذلك فيكون مضموناً عليه. وكذلك لو أخذ عبداً على أن يقرضه ألفاً هلك العبد، فإن كانت قيمته أقل من ألف ضمن قيمته لأنه بجهة الرهن مقبوض فصار كالمقبوض بحقيقة الرهن لأن المقبوض على جهة الشيء كالمقبوض على الشراء.
If a woman takes a pawn for her dower and then her husband divorces her before consummation, and then the pawn perishes, it perishes for half the dower because the dower has fallen, so it becomes like a discharge from the debt. If the mortgagee receives his right and then the pawn perishes in his possession, and he did not prevent him from taking it and its value equals the debt, he must return what he received because the debt did not fall by receipt in some respects concerning some rulings, even though it fell regarding the right of claim as we stated, so he becomes a recipient of what he received. After having once received it constructively by destruction, he is obliged to return what he received later. If the debt was a loan of food, and the debtor buys it from the creditor with dirhams and pays them to the mortgagee, and then the pawn perishes, the mortgagee must return the like of that food, and it becomes clear from this issue that the mortgagee becomes a recipient at the time of destruction, not at the time of receipt, because if he had become a recipient from the time of receipt, the sale would not be permissible because there would be nothing in the debtor's liability. A third party pays the mortgagee's debt voluntarily, and then the pawn perishes in the mortgagee's hand: he must return the money to the volunteer because he received the debt from the debtor by destruction after having received it from the volunteer, so that is obligatory upon him, just as if he had received it from the debtor and then the pawn perished. The mortgagor and mortgagee agree that there is no debt after having agreed that it was one thousand, and the pawn perishes: the mortgagee must return the thousand because at the time of destruction the pawn was guaranteed by the debt, since they did not agree that there was no debt before destruction; so the mortgagee became a recipient of the debt constructively by destruction, so it is as if he actually received it. If they agree that there was no debt before destruction, the scholars differ: some say it is a trust because the pawn was taken for a guaranteed debt whose obligation was presumed, so the pawn became guaranteed by a presumed debt; when the presumption is removed by their agreement that there is no debt, the guarantee is removed, just as if it were removed by discharge and gift. Others say he is liable because the presumption of the debt's obligation has not been removed by their agreement that there is no debt, because their agreement on the non-existence of the debt does not prevent them from agreeing on its existence afterwards, since it is possible that they will remember later that there was a debt on him; and if the presumption of obligation remains, it remains guaranteed upon him, because that by which the guarantee is established, which is the presumption of borrowing from him in the second scenario due to his preventing the borrowing, has not been removed, as it is possible that he lent him afterwards, so it would be guaranteed upon him. Similarly, if someone takes a slave on condition that he lend him one thousand, and the slave perishes: if its value is less than one thousand, he is liable for its value, because it is possessed by way of pawn, so it becomes like a pawn possessed truly, because that which is possessed by way of a thing is like that possessed by purchase.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage presents several distinct rulings (sub-cases) related to the destruction of a pawn after the debt has been discharged through various means other than the creditor's direct forgiveness. The author presents each case as a chapter or sub-issue within the broader discussion of pawn destruction. The first case involves a woman who takes a pawn for her mahr (dower) and is divorced before consummation, which reduces the mahr to half. The pawn then perishes: it perishes for half the mahr because the mahr has fallen (sagata), analogous to a discharge (bara'ah). The second case: if the mortgagee actually receives his debt (e.g., payment) but the pawn perishes in his hand without negligence, he must return what he received because the debt is not considered fully satisfied by receipt in all respects; the destruction of the pawn constructively makes him a recipient again. The third case: if the debt is a loan of food and the debtor buys that food from the creditor (with dirhams) and pays the creditor, then the pawn perishes, the creditor must return the like of the food (mithl) because he becomes a recipient at the moment of destruction, not at the earlier payment, since if he had become a recipient at the earlier payment, the sale would be invalid (the debtor's liability would be empty). The fourth case: a third party (ajnabi) pays off the mortgagee's debt voluntarily; then the pawn perishes: the mortgagee must return the money to the volunteer because the destruction of the pawn is treated as if the mortgagee received the debt from the debtor (after having received it from the third party), so he owes that amount to the volunteer. The fifth case: the two parties (mortgagor and mortgagee) agree that there is no debt after having previously agreed that it was one thousand; the pawn perishes: the mortgagee must return the thousand because the pawn was guaranteed by the debt at the time of destruction (since they only agreed to no debt later). Then another scenario: if they agree that there was no debt before destruction, there is an ikhtilaf (dispute) among the scholars. Some say the pawn is an amanah (trust) because it was based on a presumed debt, and when the presumption vanishes, the guarantee vanishes. Others say the mortgagee is liable because the presumption of a debt remains (they might later recall a debt), so the guarantee persists. The sixth case: someone takes a slave on condition that the other lends him one thousand, then the slave perishes: if the slave's value is less than one thousand, the taker is liable for the value because the possession is analogous to pawn possession. Each of these cases illustrates how the timing and nature of debt discharge affect the liability for the pawn's destruction.

Key Terms
صداق (sadaq): Dower; the bridal gift that becomes half upon divorce before consummation.
سقط (sagata): Fell; the debt is reduced or discharged.
براءة (bara'ah): Discharge; release from a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the pawn perish for half the dower in this case?
A) Because the husband paid half the dower
B) Because the dower is halved by divorce, making the pawn treated as if partially discharged
C) Because the pawn was worth half the dower
D) Because the wife agreed to forgive half

Key Takeaway
When a pawn's underlying debt is legally reduced before destruction, the pawn is treated as perishing for the discharged portion.

Mortgagee Receives Debt Then Pawn Perishes
Sub-ruling on pawn destruction after mortgagee receives payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mortgagee who receives the debt payment must return it if the pawn later perishes, and distinguish constructive receipt from actual receipt.

Core Idea
Receipt of the debt does not fully satisfy it; later destruction of the pawn creates a constructive receipt requiring return of the payment.

This lesson addresses a subtle situation: the mortgagee actually receives payment of the debt, but before the pawn is returned, the pawn perishes. The Hanafi ruling is that the mortgagee must return the payment because the pawn's destruction is treated as a constructive receipt of the debt from the mortgagor, making the earlier receipt redundant.

Guided Path
1
Understand the sequence
Debt exists, pawn is held. Mortgagee receives payment (the debt is paid). Before the pawn is returned, the pawn perishes in the mortgagee's possession.
The mortgagee now has both the payment and the destroyed pawn.
2
Identify the legal issue
Is the mortgagee entitled to keep the payment? The destruction of the pawn implies the mortgagee has 'received' the debt from the pawn itself, so the earlier payment becomes a double receipt.
The debt is considered satisfied by the pawn's destruction.
3
Apply the ruling
The mortgagee must return the payment he received, because the pawn's destruction is treated as a constructive receipt of the debt from the mortgagor.
This is as if he collected the debt twice.
4
Distinguish from actual receipt
If the pawn had been returned before destruction, the mortgagee would keep the payment. But because the pawn was still in his hand, its destruction counts as satisfaction.
The rule prevents double satisfaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أخذت المرأة رهناً بصداقها ثم طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها ثم هلك الرهن هلك بنصف الصداق لأن الصداق قد سقط فصار كالبراءة عن الدين. ولو قبض المرتهن حقه ثم هلك الرهن عنده ولم يمنعه من قبضه وقيمته مثل الدين رد ما قبض لأن الدين لم يسقط لاستيفاء من وجه في حق بعض الأحكام وإن سقط في حق المطالبة لما بينا فصار مستوفياً ما قبض. بعدما استوفاه مرة حكماً بالهلاك فيلزمه رد ما قبض آخراً. ولو كان الدين طعاماً قرضاً فاشتراه من هو عليه بدراهم ودفعها إلى المرتهن ثم هلك الرهن فعلى المرتهن رد مثل ذلك الطعام وتبين بهذه المسألة أن المرتهن يصير مستوفياً وقت الهلاك دون القبض لأنه لو صار مستوفياً من وقت القبض لما جاز البيع لأنه ليس في ذمة الراهن شيء. قضى أجنبي دين المرتهن تطوعاً ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن رد يرد المال على المتطوع لأنه استوفى الدين من الراهن بالهلاك بعدما استوفاه من المتطوع فيجب عليه ذلك كما إذا استوفاه من الغريم ثم هلك الرهن. تصادق الراهن والمرتهن أن لا دين بعد أن اتفقا أنه ألف وهلك الرهن فعلى المرتهن أن يرد الألف لأن الرهن حين هلك كان مضموناً بالدين لأنهما لم يتصادقا أن لا قبل الهلاك فصار المرتهن مستوفياً للدين حكماً بالهلاك فصار كما لو استوفاه حقيقة، ولو تصادقا أن لا دين قبل الهلاك اختلف المشايخ فيه قيل يملك أمانة لأن الرهن حصل بدين مضمون يتوهم وجوبه فصار الرهن مضموناً بدين مظنون، فإذا زال التوهم بالتصادق على أن لا دين يزول الضمان كما لو زال بالإبراء والهبة وقيل يضمن لأنه توهم وجوب الدين لم يزل تصادقهما على أن لا دين لأن تصادقهما على عدم الدين لا يمنعهما عن التصادق على الوجوب بعد ذلك لجواز أن يتذكرا بعد ما تصادقا أنه كان عليه دين وإن بقي توهم الوجوب بقي مضموناً عليه لأن ما به يثبت الضمان وهو توهم الاقتراض منه في الثاني بامتناعه الاقتراض لم يزل الجواز أن يكون أقرضه بعد ذلك فيكون مضموناً عليه. وكذلك لو أخذ عبداً على أن يقرضه ألفاً هلك العبد، فإن كانت قيمته أقل من ألف ضمن قيمته لأنه بجهة الرهن مقبوض فصار كالمقبوض بحقيقة الرهن لأن المقبوض على جهة الشيء كالمقبوض على الشراء.

Then another scenario: if they agree that there was no debt before destruction, there is an ikhtilaf (dispute) among the scholars. Some say the pawn is an amanah (trust) because it was based on a presumed debt, and when the presumption vanishes, the guarantee vanishes. Others say the mortgagee is liable because the presumption of a debt remains (they might later recall a debt), so the guarantee persists. The sixth case: someone takes a slave on condition that the other lends him one thousand, then the slave perishes: if the slave's value is less than one thousand, the taker is liable for the value because the possession is analogous to pawn possession. Each of these cases illustrates how the timing and nature of debt discharge affect the liability for the pawn's destruction.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Actual physical receipt; here, receipt of the debt payment.
استيفاء (istifa'): Receipt or collection of the debt; both actual and constructive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why must the mortgagee return the payment after the pawn perishes?
A) Because the pawn was worth less than the debt
B) Because the destruction is treated as constructive receipt, making the payment a double collection
C) Because the mortgagor can change his mind
D) Because the mortgagee was negligent

Key Takeaway
Payment of the debt does not automatically end the pawn's guarantee; destruction of the pawn after payment requires the mortgagee to return the payment.

Debt of Food, Third-Party Payment, and Agreement on No Debt
Multiple sub-rulings illustrating constructive receipt and presumption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain rulings for pawn destruction after a food loan purchase, after a third-party pays the debt, and when both parties agree there is no debt (with the ikhtilaf).

Core Idea
The timing of debt discharge relative to pawn destruction determines liability; constructive receipt and presumption of debt play key roles.

This lesson covers three additional scenarios from the passage: (1) a debt of food where the debtor buys the food back and pays, then the pawn perishes; (2) a third party voluntarily pays the mortgagee, then the pawn perishes; and (3) the mortgagor and mortgagee agree that there was no debt (either before or after destruction). Each illustrates how the law treats constructive receipt and presumption.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the food loan scenario
The debt is a loan of food (e.g., 100 kg of wheat). The debtor buys that food from the creditor with dirhams and pays. Then the pawn perishes. The mortgagee must return the like of the food (mithl) because the destruction is treated as constructive receipt at that moment, not at the time of the earlier purchase/sale.
This shows that the earlier transaction did not fully discharge the debt; the pawn still secures it.
2
Analyze the third-party payment scenario
A third party volunteers to pay the mortgagee the debt. Then the pawn perishes. The mortgagee must return the money to the volunteer because the destruction is constructive receipt from the debtor, making the volunteer's payment a double payment.
The volunteer steps into the shoes of the debtor?
3
Analyze the agreement (tasadiq) scenarios
Two sub-scenarios: (a) They agree after destruction that there is no debt (but had previously agreed it was 1,000). The mortgagee must return the 1,000 because at destruction the pawn was guaranteed by the known debt. (b) They agree before destruction that there is no debt. There is ikhtilaf: some say the pawn is a trust (amanah) because the presumption of debt is removed; others say the mortgagee is still liable because the presumption could return.
The ikhtilaf centers on whether the presumption of debt persists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أخذت المرأة رهناً بصداقها ثم طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها ثم هلك الرهن هلك بنصف الصداق لأن الصداق قد سقط فصار كالبراءة عن الدين. ولو قبض المرتهن حقه ثم هلك الرهن عنده ولم يمنعه من قبضه وقيمته مثل الدين رد ما قبض لأن الدين لم يسقط لاستيفاء من وجه في حق بعض الأحكام وإن سقط في حق المطالبة لما بينا فصار مستوفياً ما قبض. بعدما استوفاه مرة حكماً بالهلاك فيلزمه رد ما قبض آخراً. ولو كان الدين طعاماً قرضاً فاشتراه من هو عليه بدراهم ودفعها إلى المرتهن ثم هلك الرهن فعلى المرتهن رد مثل ذلك الطعام وتبين بهذه المسألة أن المرتهن يصير مستوفياً وقت الهلاك دون القبض لأنه لو صار مستوفياً من وقت القبض لما جاز البيع لأنه ليس في ذمة الراهن شيء. قضى أجنبي دين المرتهن تطوعاً ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن رد يرد المال على المتطوع لأنه استوفى الدين من الراهن بالهلاك بعدما استوفاه من المتطوع فيجب عليه ذلك كما إذا استوفاه من الغريم ثم هلك الرهن. تصادق الراهن والمرتهن أن لا دين بعد أن اتفقا أنه ألف وهلك الرهن فعلى المرتهن أن يرد الألف لأن الرهن حين هلك كان مضموناً بالدين لأنهما لم يتصادقا أن لا قبل الهلاك فصار المرتهن مستوفياً للدين حكماً بالهلاك فصار كما لو استوفاه حقيقة، ولو تصادقا أن لا دين قبل الهلاك اختلف المشايخ فيه قيل يملك أمانة لأن الرهن حصل بدين مضمون يتوهم وجوبه فصار الرهن مضموناً بدين مظنون، فإذا زال التوهم بالتصادق على أن لا دين يزول الضمان كما لو زال بالإبراء والهبة وقيل يضمن لأنه توهم وجوب الدين لم يزل تصادقهما على أن لا دين لأن تصادقهما على عدم الدين لا يمنعهما عن التصادق على الوجوب بعد ذلك لجواز أن يتذكرا بعد ما تصادقا أنه كان عليه دين وإن بقي توهم الوجوب بقي مضموناً عليه لأن ما به يثبت الضمان وهو توهم الاقتراض منه في الثاني بامتناعه الاقتراض لم يزل الجواز أن يكون أقرضه بعد ذلك فيكون مضموناً عليه. وكذلك لو أخذ عبداً على أن يقرضه ألفاً هلك العبد، فإن كانت قيمته أقل من ألف ضمن قيمته لأنه بجهة الرهن مقبوض فصار كالمقبوض بحقيقة الرهن لأن المقبوض على جهة الشيء كالمقبوض على الشراء.
If a woman takes a pawn for her dower and then her husband divorces her before consummation, and then the pawn perishes, it perishes for half the dower because the dower has fallen, so it becomes like a discharge from the debt. If the mortgagee receives his right and then the pawn perishes in his possession, and he did not prevent him from taking it and its value equals the debt, he must return what he received because the debt did not fall by receipt in some respects concerning some rulings, even though it fell regarding the right of claim as we stated, so he becomes a recipient of what he received. After having once received it constructively by destruction, he is obliged to return what he received later. If the debt was a loan of food, and the debtor buys it from the creditor with dirhams and pays them to the mortgagee, and then the pawn perishes, the mortgagee must return the like of that food, and it becomes clear from this issue that the mortgagee becomes a recipient at the time of destruction, not at the time of receipt, because if he had become a recipient from the time of receipt, the sale would not be permissible because there would be nothing in the debtor's liability. A third party pays the mortgagee's debt voluntarily, and then the pawn perishes in the mortgagee's hand: he must return the money to the volunteer because he received the debt from the debtor by destruction after having received it from the volunteer, so that is obligatory upon him, just as if he had received it from the debtor and then the pawn perished. The mortgagor and mortgagee agree that there is no debt after having agreed that it was one thousand, and the pawn perishes: the mortgagee must return the thousand because at the time of destruction the pawn was guaranteed by the debt, since they did not agree that there was no debt before destruction; so the mortgagee became a recipient of the debt constructively by destruction, so it is as if he actually received it. If they agree that there was no debt before destruction, the scholars differ: some say it is a trust because the pawn was taken for a guaranteed debt whose obligation was presumed, so the pawn became guaranteed by a presumed debt; when the presumption is removed by their agreement that there is no debt, the guarantee is removed, just as if it were removed by discharge and gift. Others say he is liable because the presumption of the debt's obligation has not been removed by their agreement that there is no debt, because their agreement on the non-existence of the debt does not prevent them from agreeing on its existence afterwards, since it is possible that they will remember later that there was a debt on him; and if the presumption of obligation remains, it remains guaranteed upon him, because that by which the guarantee is established, which is the presumption of borrowing from him in the second scenario due to his preventing the borrowing, has not been removed, as it is possible that he lent him afterwards, so it would be guaranteed upon him. Similarly, if someone takes a slave on condition that he lend him one thousand, and the slave perishes: if its value is less than one thousand, he is liable for its value, because it is possessed by way of pawn, so it becomes like a pawn possessed truly, because that which is possessed by way of a thing is like that possessed by purchase.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage presents several distinct rulings (sub-cases) related to the destruction of a pawn after the debt has been discharged through various means other than the creditor's direct forgiveness. The author presents each case as a chapter or sub-issue within the broader discussion of pawn destruction. The first case involves a woman who takes a pawn for her mahr (dower) and is divorced before consummation, which reduces the mahr to half. The pawn then perishes: it perishes for half the mahr because the mahr has fallen (sagata), analogous to a discharge (bara'ah). The second case: if the mortgagee actually receives his debt (e.g., payment) but the pawn perishes in his hand without negligence, he must return what he received because the debt is not considered fully satisfied by receipt in all respects; the destruction of the pawn constructively makes him a recipient again. The third case: if the debt is a loan of food and the debtor buys that food from the creditor (with dirhams) and pays the creditor, then the pawn perishes, the creditor must return the like of the food (mithl) because he becomes a recipient at the moment of destruction, not at the earlier payment, since if he had become a recipient at the earlier payment, the sale would be invalid (the debtor's liability would be empty). The fourth case: a third party (ajnabi) pays off the mortgagee's debt voluntarily; then the pawn perishes: the mortgagee must return the money to the volunteer because the destruction of the pawn is treated as if the mortgagee received the debt from the debtor (after having received it from the third party), so he owes that amount to the volunteer. The fifth case: the two parties (mortgagor and mortgagee) agree that there is no debt after having previously agreed that it was one thousand; the pawn perishes: the mortgagee must return the thousand because the pawn was guaranteed by the debt at the time of destruction (since they only agreed to no debt later). Then another scenario: if they agree that there was no debt before destruction, there is an ikhtilaf (dispute) among the scholars. Some say the pawn is an amanah (trust) because it was based on a presumed debt, and when the presumption vanishes, the guarantee vanishes. Others say the mortgagee is liable because the presumption of a debt remains (they might later recall a debt), so the guarantee persists. The sixth case: someone takes a slave on condition that the other lends him one thousand, then the slave perishes: if the slave's value is less than one thousand, the taker is liable for the value because the possession is analogous to pawn possession. Each of these cases illustrates how the timing and nature of debt discharge affect the liability for the pawn's destruction.

Key Terms
تصادق (tasadiq): Mutual agreement; here, both parties affirm a fact about the debt.
توهم (tawahhum): Presumption; the presumed existence of a debt that justifies the pawn's guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the agreement case where both parties agree after destruction that there was no debt (but had previously agreed it was 1,000), what is the ruling?
A) The pawn is a trust (amanah)
B) The mortgagee must return the 1,000
C) The mortgagee keeps the pawn and the debt is cancelled
D) The mortgagee must pay the value of the pawn to the mortgagor

Key Takeaway
The timing of a debt-related agreement relative to pawn destruction is crucial; constructive receipt and presumption of debt determine liability.

Slave Taken on Condition of Lending
Final sub-ruling on a pawn-like arrangement for a future loan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when a slave is taken as a pawn-like security for a promise to lend, and identify the grounds for liability analogous to pawn.

Core Idea
Taking an item as security for a future loan makes the holder liable for its value, even though no loan was actually given.

This final sub-case from the passage examines a scenario where someone takes a slave (or any item) as a 'pawn' in exchange for a promise to lend money. The promise is not fulfilled, but the slave perishes. The ruling is that the taker is liable for the slave's value, because the possession is analogous to pawn possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the arrangement
A takes B's slave on the condition that A will lend B 1,000. No loan is actually given yet. The slave is in A's possession.
This is a future loan promised.
2
Determine the nature of possession
The slave is taken 'by way of pawn' (bijah al-rahn). Even though no effective lending occurred, the possession is treated as pawn possession.
The condition creates a security interest.
3
Apply the ruling on destruction
If the slave perishes, the taker (A) is liable for its value, up to the amount of the promised loan (1,000). If the slave's value is less than 1,000, he pays the value.
This is like a pawn where the mortgagee is liable for destruction.
4
Understand the analogy
The text says 'because that which is possessed by way of a thing is like that possessed by purchase.' Here, possession by way of pawn creates guarantee.
The possession itself creates liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Pawn in Salam (Forward Sale) and Rescission
Rulings on pawn destruction after rescission of a salam contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a pawn after rescission or settlement in a salam contract and explain the distinction between qiyas and istihsan in this context.

Core Idea
A pawn taken for a salam commodity secures the substitute when the contract is rescinded or settled, by istihsan.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines nuanced scenarios where a pawn is taken in a salam (forward sale) contract and later the parties rescind or settle. Understanding the interplay between qiyas and istihsan is crucial to determine whether the pawn remains valid for the new obligation. The Hanafi school resolves the tension by preferring istihsan, preserving the security interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts and pawn
Recognize that a salam contract involves advance payment for future delivery, and a pawn may be taken to secure the commodity (muslam fihi). Then the parties may mutually rescind (tafasukh) or settle (sulh) on the principal (ra's al-maal).
The pawn is taken as security for the salam commodity.
2
Outline the first two scenarios
In the first scenario, after salam for food with a pawn, mutual rescission occurs. The mortgagee may detain the pawn until he receives back the principal because the food obligation remains until then. In the second scenario, a sale and rescission of a slave: the buyer may detain the sold object until he receives the price.
Contrast with ibra (discharge) where the pawn is released.
3
Analyze the third scenario: settlement on principal
A salam of 500 for food, pawn of a slave, then settlement (sulh) on the principal. The qiyas view says the pawn is not valid for the principal because it is a new debt. Istihsan says the pawn remains valid because the principal stands in place of the food.
This is the key qiyas vs istihsan dispute.
4
Understand the reasoning behind istihsan
Istihsan uses analogy (qiyas khafi) to the case of a pawn for a usurped object: the pawn secures the value which replaces the object. Similarly, the principal is a substitute for the food, so the pawn applies to it.
The illa (effective cause) is substitution: the new debt stands in place of the original obligation.
5
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is istihsan. Therefore, after settlement, the pawn remains valid and secures the principal. If the pawn perishes after the principal is received, the mortgagee must compensate with the like of the food and take the principal.
This ensures the pawn is not prematurely released, protecting the creditor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أسلم في طعام وأخذ به رهناً ثم تفاسخا العقد كان له أن يحبس الرهن سوم حتى يقبض برأس المال لأن رأس المال يدل على المسلم فيه فظهر أن الرهن في حق البدل، فإن هلك الرهن في يده هلك بالطعام لأنه كان مضموناً بالطعام وبالفسخ لم يسقط الطعام أصلاً ما لم يصل إليه رأس المال فبقي مضموناً به كما كان بخلاف ما لو أبرأه عن الدين لأن هناك سقط الضمان أصلاً لسقوط الدين أصلاً. ولو اشترى عبداً ثم تقابضا ثم تفاسخاً كان للمشتري أن يحبس المبيع حتى يستوفي الثمن لأنه عند الفسخ نزل منزلة البائع، وكذلك لو أسلم المبيع وأخذ بالثمن رهناً ثم تقايلا كان له أن يحبس الرهن حتى يقبض المبيع فإن هلك الرهن في يده هلك بالثمن على ما بينا أسلم خمسمائة في طعام فرهن به عبداً يساوي الطعام وقبضه ثم صالح على رأس المال فالقياس أن لا يقبض الراهن العبد ورأس المال دين عليه . الاستحسان يجعل رهناً بدينه ويكون مضموناً. وجه القياس أن رأس المال غير المسلم فيه حقيقة وحكماً لأنه ليس ببدل عن الطعام لأن الطعام وجب بالعقد ورأس المال وجب بالإقالة وهما ضدان فما وجب بأحدهما لا بدلاً عن الآخر فالرهن بالطعام لا يكون رهناً. وجه الاستحسان رأس المال بدل عن المسلم فيه قائم مقامه لأنه كان بدلاً له في العقد وبالإقالة والصلح لما سقط حقه في المسلم فيه عاد حقه إلى بدله لأنه وإن كان ديناً حادثاً لكن لما قام مقام المسلم إثباتاً وإسقاطاً فالرهن بالمسلم فيه يكون رهناً بما قام مقامه كالرهن بالمغصوب رهن بقيمته لأنها قائمة مقامه فإذا استوفى رأس المال ثم هلك عنده العبد من غير صنع يعطيه المرتهن مثل الطعام الذي كان له على المسلم إليه ويأخذ منه رأس المال
If someone makes a salam (forward sale) in food and takes a pawn for it, and then they mutually rescind (tafasukha) the contract, he may detain the pawn as security until he receives the principal (ra's al-maal) because the principal indicates the subject matter (muslam fihi), so it appears that the pawn secures the substitute. If the pawn perishes in his hand, it perishes for the food, because it was guaranteed by the food, and by rescission the food does not fall at all until the principal reaches him, so it remains guaranteed by it as before, unlike if he discharged him from the debt because there the guarantee falls completely with the fall of the debt. If someone buys a slave, and then they exchange possession (taqabada) and then rescind, the buyer may detain the sold object until he receives the price, because at rescission he takes the position of the seller. Similarly, if someone sells the bought object and takes a pawn for the price, and then they mutually annul (taqayala), he may detain the pawn until he receives the sold object. If the pawn perishes in his hand, it perishes for the price as we explained. If someone makes a salam of five hundred in food and pawns a slave equal to the food and takes possession, and then settles (salah) on the principal: by qiyas, the pawner should not take the slave and the principal remains a debt on him. By istihsan, it is made a pawn for his debt and becomes guaranteed. The basis of qiyas is that the principal is not the subject matter in reality or legally, because it is not a substitute for the food, since the food was obligated by the contract and the principal was obligated by the rescission (iqala), and they are opposites; so what is obligated by one is not a substitute for the other, so the pawn for the food is not a pawn. The basis of istihsan is that the principal is a substitute for the muslam fihi, standing in its place, because it was a substitute for it in the contract, and by the rescission and settlement, when his right to the muslam fihi fell, his right returned to its substitute; although it is a newly incurred debt, since it stands in the place of the muslam fihi in establishment and removal, the pawn for the muslam fihi becomes a pawn for what stands in its place, like a pawn for a usurped object: a pawn for its value, because the value stands in its place. So if he receives the principal and then the slave perishes in his hand without his action, the mortgagee gives him the like of the food that was due to him from the seller, and takes the principal from him.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage addresses complex issues related to pawns taken in salam (forward sale) contracts when the contract is later rescinded or settled. The author presents three scenarios. The first scenario: after a salam contract for food, a pawn is taken; then the parties mutually rescind (tafasukh). In this case, the mortgagee (creditor/ buyer) may detain the pawn until he receives back the principal (the price he paid). The pawn remains secured for the food because rescission does not cancel the food obligation until the principal is returned. This is contrasted with pure debt discharge (ibra), where the pawn's guarantee ends entirely. The second scenario: if someone buys a slave and rescinds after being possessed, he may detain the slave until he gets his price back; similarly, if he sells that slave and takes a pawn for the price, then annuls (taqayul), he may detain the pawn until he gets the sold object back. The third and longest scenario: a person makes salam (advance payment) of 500 dirhams for food, pawns a slave equal in value, takes possession, then settles (sulh) on the principal (i.e., cancels the salam and agrees to get his principal back). Here, qiyas says the pawn is not valid for the principal because the principal is a new debt, not a substitute for the food. Istihsan says the principal stands in place of the food, so the pawn remains valid for it, analogous to a pawn for a usurped object which secures its value. The author then explains the application: if the mortgagee receives the principal, then the pawned slave perishes, he must give the mortgagor the like of the food (the original salam commodity) and take the principal (i.e., he effectively swaps the pawn for the debt). This entire passage shows the Hanafi use of istihsan to preserve the security when the original purpose is transformed into a substitute.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): Forward sale: a sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later. In this passage, the pawn secures the commodity (muslam fihi).
تفاسخ (tafasukh): Mutual rescission of a contract; the parties agree to dissolve the contract and return to the original positions.
صلح (sulh): Settlement or compromise; here, the parties settle on the principal (ra's al-maal) instead of the food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the salam scenario where the parties settle on ra's al-maal (principal), what does istihsan rule regarding the pawn?
A) The pawn becomes invalid because the original debt is gone.
B) The pawn remains valid and secures the new debt (ra's al-maal).
C) The pawn is split between the two debts.
D) The pawn is returned to the mortgagor.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a pawn securing a salam commodity remains effective even after rescission or settlement, because the substitute (principal) stands in place of the commodity by istihsan.
