The Heart of Silver Pawn: Ruling When Pawn Destroyed Before Loan
Clarifies ruling when a specified pawn is destroyed before loan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pawn is destroyed before the loan is given, and explain the legal reasoning based on the analogy to goods received on approval.

Core Idea
A pawn destroyed before the loan is given is guaranteed at the agreed loan amount.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from al-Mabsut: a pawn of a 'heart of silver' given as security for a loan of one dirham, which is destroyed before the loan is disbursed. Understanding this ruling clarifies the principle that a pledge received as security is guaranteed, even if the loan has not yet been provided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? A pawn (rahn) of a heart of silver given on condition of a loan of one dirham. The pawn is destroyed before the loan is given. The ruling: the mortgagee must pay one dirham.
The loan amount is specified (one dirham), so that amount is due.
2
Locate the dalil
The text states the reasoning: 'because it was received on the basis of pawn, and what is received on the basis of pawn is like what is received on the actual pawn, like what is received on the basis of purchase negotiation.' This analogy (qiyas) to goods received on approval (sawm al-shira') is the basis.
The analogy equates a pawn received on condition of a loan to goods received for inspection, which are guaranteed at the agreed price.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The pawn is received as a pledge (rahn). In Hanafi fiqh, anything received as a pledge is a guarantee (daman) for the debt. If the loan is specified, the guarantee is the loan amount. Even though the loan was not yet given, the pawn was received on that condition, so it is as if the loan was given.
The key phrase: 'كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء' (like what is received on purchase negotiation) indicates the guarantee is by the agreed sum.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no direct ikhtilaf in this specific sub-case, but the general principle that a pawn is guaranteed when destroyed applies universally among Hanafi scholars.
The dispute arises in the next sub-case (unspecified loan) which is covered in a separate lesson.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The ruling from al-Mabsut is standard Hanafi position. No tarjih needed as it is straightforward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعرض المؤلف لمسألة القلب قال في المبسوط : رهن قلب فضة على أن يقرضه درهماً فهلك قبل أن يقرضه يعطيه درهماً لأنه مقبوض على جهة الرهن والمقبوض بجهة الرهن كالمقبوض على حقيقة الرهن كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. قال على أن أقرضه شيئاً ولم يسم شيئاً فهلك يعطيه ما شاء لأنه بالهلاك صار مستوفياً شيئاً فصار كأنه عند الهلاك. قال وجب لفلان علي شيء ولو قال امسكه رهناً بنفقة تعطيها إياه لأنه مستوفياً مالاً مجهولاً بالهلاك، ولو قال أمسكه رهناً بدراهم يلزمه ثلاثة يصير لأن أقل الجمع ثلاثة كما لو قال لفلان علي دراهم. وفي المنتقى : ولو رهنه رهناً على أن يقرضه ولم يسم القرض قال يعطيه المرتهن ما شاء، فإن قال أعطيك فلساً قال محمد رحمه الله تعالى : لا أستحسن أقل من درهم لأنه مقبوض على سوم الرهن ولا تسمية في القرض فلا يمكن اعتبار قيمته إذ لا تقدير في القرض فيعطيه ما شاء لأن الإبهام جاء من قبله ولا يصدق في أقل من لأن العادة لم تجر في اقتراض أقل من درهم، وهذه المسألة المذكورة في عيون مسائل لأبي درهم . وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى : لو قال رجل اقرضني وخذ هذا الرهن ولم يسم القرض فأخذ الرهن فضاع ولم يقرضه قال عليه قيمة الرهن. ولو رهن ثوباً فقال أمسكه بعشرين درهماً فهلك الثوب عند المرتهن قبل أن يعطيه شيئاً فعليه قيمة الثوب إلا أن تجاوز قيمته عشرين لأن الرهن مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومن الدين. رهن دابتين على أن يقرضه مائة وقيمة أحدهما خمسون والأخرى ثلاثون فقبض وقبض التي قيمتها خمسون فهلكت برد خمسين لأنه مضمون بالقيمة لا بالمسمى كالمقبوض بجهة البيع فإن بداله أن يأخذ الأخرى ويقرضه له ذلك ولا يجبر على القرض لأن الرهن لازم من في جانب الراهن، فما شرط على الراهن في الرهن يكون لازماً وفي حق المرتهن غير لازم فما شرطه على المرتهن لا يكون لازماً والقرض مشروط على المرتهن فيكون لازماً في حقه. ولو هلكت إحداهما عند الراهن واختلفا في قيمة التي هلكت عند المرتهن فالقول للمرتهن لأن الراهن يدعي على المرتهن زيادة ضمان وهو ينكر، فإن بقيت إحداهما ينظر إلى قيمة الباقي فتظهر قيمة الهالك فلا يلتفت إلى اختلافهما لأنه أمكن معرفة ما وقع التنازع فيه لا من جهتهما
And the author did not address the case of the 'heart'. He said in al-Mabsut: He pawned a heart of silver on condition that he would lend him a dirham, and it was destroyed before he lent it; he gives him a dirham because it was received on the basis of pawn, and what is received on the basis of pawn is like what is received on the actual pawn, like what is received on the basis of purchase negotiation. He said: on condition that I lend him something, and he did not specify anything, then it was destroyed; he gives him whatever he wishes because by destruction he becomes having received something, so it becomes as if at the time of destruction. He said: something is owed to so-and-so on me. And if he said: hold this pawn for an expenditure that you give him, because he has received unknown wealth by destruction. And if he said: hold this pawn for dirhams that are owed to him, three become binding because the least of a plural is three, just as if he said: I owe dirhams to so-and-so. In al-Muntaqa: And if he pawned a pawn on condition that he would lend him, and did not name the loan, he said: the mortgagee gives him whatever he wishes. If he said: I give you a fals, Muhammad said: I do not deem it good (istihsan) less than a dirham, because it is received on the basis of pawn negotiation, and there is no specification in the loan, so its value cannot be considered since there is no estimation in the loan, so he gives him whatever he wishes because the ambiguity came from him, and he is not believed for less than a dirham because custom does not allow borrowing less than a dirham. And this case is mentioned in 'Uyun Masa'il of Abu Dirham. And al-Mu'alla related from Abu Yusuf: If a man said: lend me and take this pawn, and did not name the loan, and he took the pawn and it was lost and he did not lend him, he said: the value of the pawn is due. And if he pawned a garment and said: hold it for twenty dirhams, and the garment was destroyed in the mortgagee's possession before he gave him anything, then the value of the garment is due unless its value exceeds twenty, because the pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. He pawned two animals on condition that he would lend him one hundred, and the value of one is fifty and the other thirty; he took and took one valued at fifty, and it was destroyed; he returns fifty because it is guaranteed by value, not by the named sum, like what is received on the basis of sale. For he may instead take the other and lend him that, and he is not compelled to lend because the pawn is binding from the side of the pledgor; whatever condition is on the pledgor in the pawn is binding, but on the mortgagee it is not binding. So whatever condition is on the mortgagee is not binding, and the loan is conditioned on the mortgagee, so it is binding on him. And if one of them was destroyed in the pledgor's possession and they differed on the value of the one destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, the statement is of the mortgagee because the pledgor claims an increase in guarantee and he denies. And if one remains, the value of the remaining is looked at, so the value of the destroyed appears, and no attention is paid to their difference because it is possible to know what the dispute is about not from their statements.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (masa'il) on various issues of pawn (rahn) where the loan amount is unspecified or partially specified. It covers: (1) Rahn of a 'heart of silver' for a loan of a dirham; if destroyed before loan, the mortgagee pays a dirham. (2) If the loan is unspecified, the mortgagee may choose any amount after destruction. (3) If the pawn is held for 'dirhams' generally, the minimum is three. (4) According to Muhammad, if the mortgagee offers a fals, it is not good (istihsan) unless at least a dirham due to custom. (5) Abu Yusuf: if the pawn is taken but loan not given, the value of pawn is due. (6) If a pawn is held for a specific amount but destroyed before loan given, the lesser of value and debt is due. (7) If two animals are pawned for a loan of 100, and one is taken and destroyed, the mortgagee pays its value. The mortgagee may choose to take the other but is not compelled to lend. (8) If one animal is destroyed with pledgor and dispute arises on value of the one with mortgagee, the mortgagee's statement is believed.

Key Terms
قلب فضة (qalb fidda): A heart of silver; a specific object used as a pawn in the example.
سوم الشراء (sawm al-shira'): Purchase negotiation; goods given for inspection with a view to purchase, which are guaranteed if destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the pawn was received on the basis of pawn, analogous to sale
B) Because the pawn was received on the basis of pawn, analogous to purchase negotiation
C) Because the loan was already given in spirit
D) Because the heart of silver is valuable

Key Takeaway
A pawn destroyed before the loan is given is guaranteed at the specified loan amount due to the analogy to goods received on approval.

Pledge for an Unspecified Loan: General Rule and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explains ruling and dispute for unspecified loan amounts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a pawn is given for an unspecified loan, distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
For an unspecified loan, the mortgagee chooses the amount, but custom sets a minimum of one dirham.

This lesson covers the scenario where a pawn is given on condition of a loan, but the loan amount is not specified. The Hanafi school has an intra-madhhab dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that the mortgagee may choose any amount but not less than a dirham due to custom, while Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the loan is not given, the value of the pawn is due. Understanding this difference is essential for applying the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The general rule from al-Muntaqa: if a pawn is given for an unspecified loan, the mortgagee may give whatever he wishes after the pawn is destroyed. The ambiguity is resolved in his favor because it came from the pledgor's failure to specify.
This is the position of Imam Muhammad.
2
Identify the dispute
Abu Yusuf differs: if the pawn is taken and the loan is not given, the mortgagee must pay the value of the pawn, not a chosen amount.
Abu Yusuf's view emphasizes the pawn's value as the guarantee.
3
Follow Muhammad's proof
Muhammad argues that because the loan amount was not specified, the mortgagee can choose, but custom (urf) dictates that less than a dirham is not borrowed, so the minimum is one dirham.
The proof is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and custom.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response to Abu Yusuf: the mortgagee is not compelled to lend; the pawn is a guarantee for a debt that is not yet due in terms of amount. The ambiguity falls back on the pledgor, so the mortgagee's choice is accepted.
The text also notes that the mortgagee is not compelled to lend (la yujbar 'ala al-qard).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Muhammad, the mortgagee can claim a small amount (but at least a dirham); under Abu Yusuf, the mortgagee must pay the full value of the pawn if the loan is not given.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view, as it is considered more in line with custom and the principle that ambiguity is attributed to the one who created it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعرض المؤلف لمسألة القلب قال في المبسوط : رهن قلب فضة على أن يقرضه درهماً فهلك قبل أن يقرضه يعطيه درهماً لأنه مقبوض على جهة الرهن والمقبوض بجهة الرهن كالمقبوض على حقيقة الرهن كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. قال على أن أقرضه شيئاً ولم يسم شيئاً فهلك يعطيه ما شاء لأنه بالهلاك صار مستوفياً شيئاً فصار كأنه عند الهلاك. قال وجب لفلان علي شيء ولو قال امسكه رهناً بنفقة تعطيها إياه لأنه مستوفياً مالاً مجهولاً بالهلاك، ولو قال أمسكه رهناً بدراهم يلزمه ثلاثة يصير لأن أقل الجمع ثلاثة كما لو قال لفلان علي دراهم. وفي المنتقى : ولو رهنه رهناً على أن يقرضه ولم يسم القرض قال يعطيه المرتهن ما شاء، فإن قال أعطيك فلساً قال محمد رحمه الله تعالى : لا أستحسن أقل من درهم لأنه مقبوض على سوم الرهن ولا تسمية في القرض فلا يمكن اعتبار قيمته إذ لا تقدير في القرض فيعطيه ما شاء لأن الإبهام جاء من قبله ولا يصدق في أقل من لأن العادة لم تجر في اقتراض أقل من درهم، وهذه المسألة المذكورة في عيون مسائل لأبي درهم . وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى : لو قال رجل اقرضني وخذ هذا الرهن ولم يسم القرض فأخذ الرهن فضاع ولم يقرضه قال عليه قيمة الرهن. ولو رهن ثوباً فقال أمسكه بعشرين درهماً فهلك الثوب عند المرتهن قبل أن يعطيه شيئاً فعليه قيمة الثوب إلا أن تجاوز قيمته عشرين لأن الرهن مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومن الدين. رهن دابتين على أن يقرضه مائة وقيمة أحدهما خمسون والأخرى ثلاثون فقبض وقبض التي قيمتها خمسون فهلكت برد خمسين لأنه مضمون بالقيمة لا بالمسمى كالمقبوض بجهة البيع فإن بداله أن يأخذ الأخرى ويقرضه له ذلك ولا يجبر على القرض لأن الرهن لازم من في جانب الراهن، فما شرط على الراهن في الرهن يكون لازماً وفي حق المرتهن غير لازم فما شرطه على المرتهن لا يكون لازماً والقرض مشروط على المرتهن فيكون لازماً في حقه. ولو هلكت إحداهما عند الراهن واختلفا في قيمة التي هلكت عند المرتهن فالقول للمرتهن لأن الراهن يدعي على المرتهن زيادة ضمان وهو ينكر، فإن بقيت إحداهما ينظر إلى قيمة الباقي فتظهر قيمة الهالك فلا يلتفت إلى اختلافهما لأنه أمكن معرفة ما وقع التنازع فيه لا من جهتهما

Key Terms
سوم الرهن (sawm al-rahn): Pawn negotiation: the context in which the pawn is received as a basis for determining liability.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: a method of deriving a ruling by preferring one analogy over another or by departing from an analogy based on a stronger evidence or custom.

Pledge for a Fixed Amount But Destroyed Before Loan: Lesser of Value and Debt
Provides a specific ruling for a pawn with a fixed debt destroyed before loan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt when the pawn is destroyed before the loan is given.

Core Idea
When a pawn is held for a fixed debt and destroyed before loan, the guarantee is the lesser of its value and the debt.

This lesson addresses a case where a pawn is given with a specific debt amount (e.g., twenty dirhams) but the pawn is destroyed before the lender gives any money. The ruling is that the mortgagee must pay the value of the pawn, unless the value exceeds the debt, in which case only the debt is due. This principle is analogous to goods received on sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
A man pawns a garment and says 'hold it for twenty dirhams.' The garment is destroyed before the mortgagee gives anything. Ruling: the mortgagee must pay the value of the garment, but if the value exceeds 20, only 20 is due.
The debt is specified (20), so it is a limit.
2
Locate the dalil
The text states: 'because the pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt.' This is a general principle (qa'ida) for pawns.
This principle applies when the pawn is destroyed before the debt is given.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The pawn is a security. If it is destroyed, the mortgagee must compensate, but the compensation cannot exceed the debt (the maximum he would have lent) nor more than the value (since the pawn's worth is the actual loss).
This prevents unjust enrichment.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no dispute in this specific sub-case; it is consistent across the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This ruling is straightforward and accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعرض المؤلف لمسألة القلب قال في المبسوط : رهن قلب فضة على أن يقرضه درهماً فهلك قبل أن يقرضه يعطيه درهماً لأنه مقبوض على جهة الرهن والمقبوض بجهة الرهن كالمقبوض على حقيقة الرهن كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. قال على أن أقرضه شيئاً ولم يسم شيئاً فهلك يعطيه ما شاء لأنه بالهلاك صار مستوفياً شيئاً فصار كأنه عند الهلاك. قال وجب لفلان علي شيء ولو قال امسكه رهناً بنفقة تعطيها إياه لأنه مستوفياً مالاً مجهولاً بالهلاك، ولو قال أمسكه رهناً بدراهم يلزمه ثلاثة يصير لأن أقل الجمع ثلاثة كما لو قال لفلان علي دراهم. وفي المنتقى : ولو رهنه رهناً على أن يقرضه ولم يسم القرض قال يعطيه المرتهن ما شاء، فإن قال أعطيك فلساً قال محمد رحمه الله تعالى : لا أستحسن أقل من درهم لأنه مقبوض على سوم الرهن ولا تسمية في القرض فلا يمكن اعتبار قيمته إذ لا تقدير في القرض فيعطيه ما شاء لأن الإبهام جاء من قبله ولا يصدق في أقل من لأن العادة لم تجر في اقتراض أقل من درهم، وهذه المسألة المذكورة في عيون مسائل لأبي درهم . وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى : لو قال رجل اقرضني وخذ هذا الرهن ولم يسم القرض فأخذ الرهن فضاع ولم يقرضه قال عليه قيمة الرهن. ولو رهن ثوباً فقال أمسكه بعشرين درهماً فهلك الثوب عند المرتهن قبل أن يعطيه شيئاً فعليه قيمة الثوب إلا أن تجاوز قيمته عشرين لأن الرهن مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومن الدين. رهن دابتين على أن يقرضه مائة وقيمة أحدهما خمسون والأخرى ثلاثون فقبض وقبض التي قيمتها خمسون فهلكت برد خمسين لأنه مضمون بالقيمة لا بالمسمى كالمقبوض بجهة البيع فإن بداله أن يأخذ الأخرى ويقرضه له ذلك ولا يجبر على القرض لأن الرهن لازم من في جانب الراهن، فما شرط على الراهن في الرهن يكون لازماً وفي حق المرتهن غير لازم فما شرطه على المرتهن لا يكون لازماً والقرض مشروط على المرتهن فيكون لازماً في حقه. ولو هلكت إحداهما عند الراهن واختلفا في قيمة التي هلكت عند المرتهن فالقول للمرتهن لأن الراهن يدعي على المرتهن زيادة ضمان وهو ينكر، فإن بقيت إحداهما ينظر إلى قيمة الباقي فتظهر قيمة الهالك فلا يلتفت إلى اختلافهما لأنه أمكن معرفة ما وقع التنازع فيه لا من جهتهما
And the author did not address the case of the 'heart'. He said in al-Mabsut: He pawned a heart of silver on condition that he would lend him a dirham, and it was destroyed before he lent it; he gives him a dirham because it was received on the basis of pawn, and what is received on the basis of pawn is like what is received on the actual pawn, like what is received on the basis of purchase negotiation. He said: on condition that I lend him something, and he did not specify anything, then it was destroyed; he gives him whatever he wishes because by destruction he becomes having received something, so it becomes as if at the time of destruction. He said: something is owed to so-and-so on me. And if he said: hold this pawn for an expenditure that you give him, because he has received unknown wealth by destruction. And if he said: hold this pawn for dirhams that are owed to him, three become binding because the least of a plural is three, just as if he said: I owe dirhams to so-and-so. In al-Muntaqa: And if he pawned a pawn on condition that he would lend him, and did not name the loan, he said: the mortgagee gives him whatever he wishes. If he said: I give you a fals, Muhammad said: I do not deem it good (istihsan) less than a dirham, because it is received on the basis of pawn negotiation, and there is no specification in the loan, so its value cannot be considered since there is no estimation in the loan, so he gives him whatever he wishes because the ambiguity came from him, and he is not believed for less than a dirham because custom does not allow borrowing less than a dirham. And this case is mentioned in 'Uyun Masa'il of Abu Dirham. And al-Mu'alla related from Abu Yusuf: If a man said: lend me and take this pawn, and did not name the loan, and he took the pawn and it was lost and he did not lend him, he said: the value of the pawn is due. And if he pawned a garment and said: hold it for twenty dirhams, and the garment was destroyed in the mortgagee's possession before he gave him anything, then the value of the garment is due unless its value exceeds twenty, because the pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. He pawned two animals on condition that he would lend him one hundred, and the value of one is fifty and the other thirty; he took and took one valued at fifty, and it was destroyed; he returns fifty because it is guaranteed by value, not by the named sum, like what is received on the basis of sale. For he may instead take the other and lend him that, and he is not compelled to lend because the pawn is binding from the side of the pledgor; whatever condition is on the pledgor in the pawn is binding, but on the mortgagee it is not binding. So whatever condition is on the mortgagee is not binding, and the loan is conditioned on the mortgagee, so it is binding on him. And if one of them was destroyed in the pledgor's possession and they differed on the value of the one destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, the statement is of the mortgagee because the pledgor claims an increase in guarantee and he denies. And if one remains, the value of the remaining is looked at, so the value of the destroyed appears, and no attention is paid to their difference because it is possible to know what the dispute is about not from their statements.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (masa'il) on various issues of pawn (rahn) where the loan amount is unspecified or partially specified. It covers: (1) Rahn of a 'heart of silver' for a loan of a dirham; if destroyed before loan, the mortgagee pays a dirham. (2) If the loan is unspecified, the mortgagee may choose any amount after destruction. (3) If the pawn is held for 'dirhams' generally, the minimum is three. (4) According to Muhammad, if the mortgagee offers a fals, it is not good (istihsan) unless at least a dirham due to custom. (5) Abu Yusuf: if the pawn is taken but loan not given, the value of pawn is due. (6) If a pawn is held for a specific amount but destroyed before loan given, the lesser of value and debt is due. (7) If two animals are pawned for a loan of 100, and one is taken and destroyed, the mortgagee pays its value. The mortgagee may choose to take the other but is not compelled to lend. (8) If one animal is destroyed with pledgor and dispute arises on value of the one with mortgagee, the mortgagee's statement is believed.

Key Terms
مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومن الدين (madmūn bi-aqalli min qīmatihi wa min al-dayn): Guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pawn is destroyed before the loan is given, and the pawn's value is less than the debt, how much does the mortgagee owe?
A) The debt amount
B) The value of the pawn
C) Half the debt
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's liability when a pawn is destroyed before the loan is the lesser of the pawn's value and the debt.

Pledge of Multiple Items: Options and Dispute Resolution
Explains rulings for multiple pawn items, options, and dispute resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings when multiple animals are pawned for a loan, including the mortgagee's option to choose another item, the binding nature of conditions, and how to resolve disputes over value.

Core Idea
When two animals are pawned for a loan, the mortgagee can choose which to take, but is not compelled to lend; if destroyed, value is due; disputes on value are resolved by the mortgagee's statement or by examination.

This lesson covers a more complex scenario: two animals pawned for a loan of one hundred dirhams, each with different values. It explores what happens if one animal is taken and destroyed, the mortgagee's option to take the other, and the rule that the mortgagee cannot be forced to lend. It also addresses dispute resolution when the animals are with different parties and values are contested.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Two animals pawned for a loan of 100. One animal (value 50) is taken by the mortgagee and destroyed. Ruling: mortgagee must pay 50 (value of that animal) because pawns are guaranteed by value, not the named sum.
The ruling is based on the principle that pawns are guaranteed by value (like goods received on sale).
2
Understand the mortgagee's option
The mortgagee may alternatively take the other animal (value 30) and lend the 100, but he is not compelled to lend. The pawn contract is binding on the pledgor, but the condition to lend is on the mortgagee, which is not binding unless he agrees.
This shows the asymmetry: conditions favorable to the mortgagee are not binding on him.
3
Apply the rules of dispute resolution
If one animal is destroyed with the pledgor and they dispute the value of the one with the mortgagee, the mortgagee's statement is believed because the pledgor is claiming an increase in guarantee.
If only one animal remains, its value can be examined to determine the value of the destroyed one, so no dispute is entertained.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
No dispute in this sub-case; it is consistent within the school.

لازم (lāzim): Binding: the pawn contract is binding on the pledgor (must give the pawn) but not on the mortgagee regarding lending.

Disputes on Value and Ownership of the Pledge
Rulings on evidentiary burden in disputes over value and ownership of a pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disputes over the value of a destroyed pledge and on claims involving third-party possessors, and apply the principle that evidence establishing liability is preferred.

Core Idea
In pledge disputes, the party whose evidence establishes liability is preferred; the mortgagee's word on value is taken after destruction.

When a pledge is destroyed, mortgagor and mortgagee may disagree on its value. Also, claims may involve a third party possessing the pledge. This passage from Bahra al-Ra'iq provides clear rulings based on the principle that evidence establishing liability is stronger than evidence negating it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenarios
Recognize that the passage covers two scenarios: (1) value after destruction, (2) a third party claiming ownership of the pledged property.
The rulings apply when the parties disagree without proof.
2
Determine the default rule for value disputes
For value after destruction, the mortgagee's statement is accepted, but the mortgagor must provide evidence if he claims a higher value.
The reasoning: the mortgagor claims an increase, so he must prove it.
3
Analyze the third-party possession scenario
When a person claims a slave in another's hand is his and that he pawned it to a third party, and the possessor claims ownership, the possessor becomes a litigant and the property is held by a trustee until the absent party appears.
If the possessor acknowledges the third party's ownership, he is not a litigant.
4
Apply the rule to the mortgagee's claim against a possessor
If the mortgagee claims the pledge is in the hand of a possessor and alleges that the possessor took it by usurpation, loan, or lease, his claim is accepted and the pledge is handed to him, provided he accuses the possessor of a wrongful act.
If no such accusation, his claim is not accepted because he has not proven the taking.
5
Understand the underlying legal principle
The common thread is that in disputes, the party who establishes liability (by evidence or consistent claim) is preferred over the one who denies it.
This is analogous to the rule in usurpation cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلف الراهن والمرتهن في قيمة الرهن بعد هلاكه فالقول للمرتهن والبينة للراهن لأن الراهن يدعي عليه زيادة وهو ينكر فكانت بينته أكثر إثباتاً. ادعى عبداً في يد غيره أنه عبده رهنه من فلان وقبضه فلان وذو اليد يقول هو عبد لي يقضي للمدعي لأن ذا اليد انتصب خصماً للمدعي لأنه ادعى الملك لنفسه ويوضع على يدي عدل حتى يحضر الغائب بخلاف ما لو أقر بالملك للغائب فقد أقر أنه ليس له حق الإمساك لأنه لا يتصور يكون ممسكاً لملك الغير بحكم النيابة. ولو ادعى المرتهن هذا والرهن غائب يدفع إليه إذا قال غصبه ذو اليد وأخذتها مني بعارية أو إجارة لأنه ادعى فعلاً على ذي اليد وأنكر ذو اليد فينصب خصماً له، فلو لم يدع على ذي اليد الأخذ من يده لا يدفع إليه لأنه لم يثبت الأخذ من يده كما لو ادعى عيناً في يد إنسان أنها ملكه اغتصبها منه وأقام ذو اليد البينة على أنها وديعة عنده لفلان تقبل بينة المدعي لأنه ادعى فعلاً عليه فانتصب خصماً له، فإن لم يدع من يده لا تقبل بينته ولا ينتصب خصماً فكذا هذا. أقر المرتهن أن في يده رهناً قيمته ألف ثم جاء بما يساوي مائة فقال لم أرهنك هذا فالقول له إذا تراجع سعر ما يساوي ألفاً إلى مائة فالقول للمرتهن لأنه إذا عرف تغير السعر فالظاهر شاهد للمرتهن. ولو قال رهنتك وهو مسلم وقال المرتهن وهو كافر فالقول للمرتهن والبينة للراهن، وكذلك القصاص والسرقة لأن الراهن يدعي عليه الإيفاء أو زيادة الإيفاء وهو ينكر فيكون القول له. قال المرتهن أخذت المال ورددت الرهن وأنكر الراهن الرد فالبينة للراهن لأن بينة الرهن تثبت الضمان على المرتهن لأن ضمان الرهن والاستيفاء لم يكن ثابتاً بالقبض السابق لأن قبض الرهن قبل الهلاك كان استيفاء في حق الحبس لا في حق ملك الغير وبالهلاك يصير قبض الاستيفاء في حق ملك الغير فلم يكن ضمان الاستيفاء ثابتاً قبل الهلاك فكانت بينته مثبتة الضمان وبينة الراهن نافية فكانت المثبتة أولى بخلاف ما لو أقام الغاصب البينة على رد المغصوب وأقام المالك البينة على الهلاك فبينة الغاصب أولى لأن ضمان الرد كان واجباً بالغصب السابق لأنه أوجب رد العين حال قيامها ورد القيمة حال هلاكها، فبينة الغاصب مثبتة البراءة عن الضمان وبينة المالك نافية للبراءة فكانت المثبتة أولى.
If the mortgagor and mortgagee differ about the value of the pledge after its destruction, the statement is that of the mortgagee, and the evidence is that of the mortgagor, because the mortgagor claims an increase against him and he denies, so his evidence is more probative. If someone claims a slave in the hand of another that it is his slave and he pawned it to so-and-so and so-and-so seized it, and the possessor says it is my slave, judgement is given for the claimant because the possessor becomes a litigant against the claimant since he claimed ownership for himself, and it is placed with a trustworthy person until the absent one appears, unlike if he acknowledged ownership for the absent one, for he has acknowledged that he has no right of retention because he cannot be imagined to hold the property of another by way of deputyship. If the mortgagee claims this while the pledge is absent, it is handed over to him if he says 'the possessor usurped it and I took it from him by loan or lease' because he claims an act against the possessor and the possessor denies, so he becomes a litigant against him. If he does not claim taking from the possessor's hand, it is not handed over to him because he has not proven the taking from his hand, as if someone claims a specific thing in the hand of a person that it is his property usurped from him, and the possessor brings evidence that it is a deposit with him for so-and-so, the claimant's evidence is accepted because he claims an act against him so he becomes a litigant; if he does not claim from his hand, his evidence is not accepted and he does not become a litigant. Similarly here. If the mortgagee acknowledges that in his hand is a pledge worth one thousand, then brings something worth one hundred and says 'I did not pawn this to you', the statement is his; if the price of what is worth one thousand decreases to one hundred, the statement is the mortgagee's because if the price change is known, the apparent circumstance testifies for the mortgagee. If he says 'I pawned to you' while he is Muslim and the mortgagee is a disbeliever, the statement is the mortgagee's and the evidence is the mortgagor's, and similarly for retaliation and theft because the mortgagor claims payment or excess payment from him and he denies, so the statement is his. If the mortgagee says 'I took the money and returned the pledge' and the mortgagor denies the return, the evidence is the mortgagor's because the mortgagor's evidence establishes liability on the mortgagee, since the liability of the pledge and satisfaction was not established by the prior seizure because the seizure before destruction was satisfaction in terms of retention not in terms of ownership of the property of another, and with destruction the seizure becomes satisfaction in terms of ownership of the property of another, so the liability of satisfaction was not established before destruction, thus his evidence establishes liability and the mortgagor's evidence negates it, so the establishing evidence is preferable, unlike if the usurper brings evidence of return of the usurped property and the owner brings evidence of destruction, for the usurper's evidence is preferable because the liability for return was made obligatory by the prior usurpation since it required return of the object while it exists and payment of its value upon destruction, so the usurper's evidence establishes freedom from liability and the owner's evidence negates freedom, so the establishing evidence is preferable.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings on disputes between mortgagor (raahin) and mortgagee (murtahin) in a pledge contract. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The first ruling: if the pledge is destroyed and they dispute its value, the mortgagee's statement is taken (because he is the one who would know the value he accepted), but the burden of proof is on the mortgagor if he claims a higher value. The reasoning is that the mortgagor is claiming an excess, so he must prove it. Next, a scenario where a person claims a slave in another's possession is his, and he claims he pawned it to a third party. If the possessor claims ownership for himself, he becomes a litigant and the slave is placed with a trustee until the absent third party appears. But if the possessor acknowledges the pledge and claims to hold it as a trustee, he is not a litigant because he admits he has no ownership claim. Then, if the mortgagee claims that the pledge is in the hands of a third party (absent), and he says the possessor took it by usurpation or loan, his claim is accepted and the pledge is handed over to him, provided he accuses the possessor of a wrongful act; otherwise not. Another ruling: the mortgagee admits the pledge is worth 1000 but then produces something worth 100; his statement about the value is accepted unless market price changes are known. If the value drops generally, the mortgagee's statement is taken because the market trend supports him. Then, if the mortgagor is Muslim and the mortgagee is non-Muslim, the mortgagee's statement is taken regarding the existence of the debt, but evidence is on the mortgagor. Finally, if the mortgagee claims he returned the pledge after collecting the debt, and the mortgagor denies, the evidence is on the mortgagor (to prove return) because the mortgagee's liability for the pledge is established by the original seizure; the mortgagee's claim of return negates that liability, so the mortgagor's evidence (establishing liability) is preferred, analogous to a case of usurpation where the usurper's evidence of return is preferred over the owner's evidence of destruction.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): The pledged property; the subject matter of the rahn contract.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The mortgagee; the person who receives the pledge.
الراهن (ar-raahin): The mortgagor; the person who gives the pledge.
ذو اليد (dhu al-yad): The possessor; the person who currently holds the property.
الخصم (al-khasm): Litigant; a party to a legal dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over the value of a destroyed pledge, whose statement is initially taken according to Hanafi law?
A) The mortgagor's
B) The mortgagee's
C) Both must provide evidence
D) The judge's estimation

Key Takeaway
In pledge disputes, the party whose evidence establishes liability is preferred; for value after destruction, the mortgagee's statement is taken unless the mortgagor proves a higher value.

Disputes on Return and Acknowledgment of Value in Pledge
Rulings on disputes over value acknowledgment, religious difference, and return of the pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on disputes regarding the mortgagee's acknowledgment of the pledge's value, claims involving religious difference, and the return of the pledge, and explain the reasoning based on the preference for evidence establishing liability.

Core Idea
When the mortgagee acknowledges the pledge's value but produces a lesser item, his word is taken; if he claims return, the mortgagor's evidence is preferred.

This lesson continues the discussion of disputes in pledge contracts. It covers cases where the mortgagee admits to holding a valuable pledge but then produces a cheaper one, when the parties differ in religion, and when the mortgagee claims to have returned the pledge after collecting the debt. The guiding principle remains that evidence establishing liability is stronger than evidence negating it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mortgagee's acknowledgment of value
If the mortgagee acknowledges holding a pledge worth 1000, then brings something worth 100 and denies it is the same, his statement is accepted unless the market price has generally dropped.
If the market price declined, the mortgagee's statement is taken because the apparent circumstance supports him.
2
Analyze the dispute when parties differ in religion
If the mortgagor is Muslim and the mortgagee is a disbeliever, and the mortgagor claims he pawned something, the mortgagee's statement is taken and the mortgagor must prove his claim.
Similarly in cases of retaliation and theft, the claim of payment is on the mortgagor.
3
Examine the dispute over return of the pledge
If the mortgagee says he took the money and returned the pledge, and the mortgagor denies, the evidence is on the mortgagor to prove the return was not made.
The reason: the mortgagor's evidence would establish the mortgagee's liability for the pledge, which is stronger than the mortgagee's claim that he is free from liability.
4
Compare with the usurpation analogy
The passage draws an analogy with a usurper who claims to have returned the usurped property; his evidence of return is preferred over the owner's evidence of destruction, because the usurper's evidence establishes freedom from liability.
In the pledge case, the situation is reversed: the mortgagor's evidence establishes liability, so it is preferred.
5
Apply the principle consistently
The common thread is that evidence which establishes a liability or right takes precedence over evidence that negates it.
This principle governs all the rulings in this passage.

ولو اختلف الراهن والمرتهن في قيمة الرهن بعد هلاكه فالقول للمرتهن والبينة للراهن لأن الراهن يدعي عليه زيادة وهو ينكر فكانت بينته أكثر إثباتاً. ادعى عبداً في يد غيره أنه عبده رهنه من فلان وقبضه فلان وذو اليد يقول هو عبد لي يقضي للمدعي لأن ذا اليد انتصب خصماً للمدعي لأنه ادعى الملك لنفسه ويوضع على يدي عدل حتى يحضر الغائب بخلاف ما لو أقر بالملك للغائب فقد أقر أنه ليس له حق الإمساك لأنه لا يتصور يكون ممسكاً لملك الغير بحكم النيابة. ولو ادعى المرتهن هذا والرهن غائب يدفع إليه إذا قال غصبه ذو اليد وأخذتها مني بعارية أو إجارة لأنه ادعى فعلاً على ذي اليد وأنكر ذو اليد فينصب خصماً له، فلو لم يدع على ذي اليد الأخذ من يده لا يدفع إليه لأنه لم يثبت الأخذ من يده كما لو ادعى عيناً في يد إنسان أنها ملكه اغتصبها منه وأقام ذو اليد البينة على أنها وديعة عنده لفلان تقبل بينة المدعي لأنه ادعى فعلاً عليه فانتصب خصماً له، فإن لم يدع من يده لا تقبل بينته ولا ينتصب خصماً فكذا هذا. أقر المرتهن أن في يده رهناً قيمته ألف ثم جاء بما يساوي مائة فقال لم أرهنك هذا فالقول له إذا تراجع سعر ما يساوي ألفاً إلى مائة فالقول للمرتهن لأنه إذا عرف تغير السعر فالظاهر شاهد للمرتهن. ولو قال رهنتك وهو مسلم وقال المرتهن وهو كافر فالقول للمرتهن والبينة للراهن، وكذلك القصاص والسرقة لأن الراهن يدعي عليه الإيفاء أو زيادة الإيفاء وهو ينكر فيكون القول له. قال المرتهن أخذت المال ورددت الرهن وأنكر الراهن الرد فالبينة للراهن لأن بينة الرهن تثبت الضمان على المرتهن لأن ضمان الرهن والاستيفاء لم يكن ثابتاً بالقبض السابق لأن قبض الرهن قبل الهلاك كان استيفاء في حق الحبس لا في حق ملك الغير وبالهلاك يصير قبض الاستيفاء في حق ملك الغير فلم يكن ضمان الاستيفاء ثابتاً قبل الهلاك فكانت بينته مثبتة الضمان وبينة الراهن نافية فكانت المثبتة أولى بخلاف ما لو أقام الغاصب البينة على رد المغصوب وأقام المالك البينة على الهلاك فبينة الغاصب أولى لأن ضمان الرد كان واجباً بالغصب السابق لأنه أوجب رد العين حال قيامها ورد القيمة حال هلاكها، فبينة الغاصب مثبتة البراءة عن الضمان وبينة المالك نافية للبراءة فكانت المثبتة أولى.
If the mortgagor and mortgagee differ about the value of the pledge after its destruction, the statement is that of the mortgagee, and the evidence is that of the mortgagor, because the mortgagor claims an increase against him and he denies, so his evidence is more probative. If someone claims a slave in the hand of another that it is his slave and he pawned it to so-and-so and so-and-so seized it, and the possessor says it is my slave, judgement is given for the claimant because the possessor becomes a litigant against the claimant since he claimed ownership for himself, and it is placed with a trustworthy person until the absent one appears, unlike if he acknowledged ownership for the absent one, for he has acknowledged that he has no right of retention because he cannot be imagined to hold the property of another by way of deputyship. If the mortgagee claims this while the pledge is absent, it is handed over to him if he says 'the possessor usurped it and I took it from him by loan or lease' because he claims an act against the possessor and the possessor denies, so he becomes a litigant against him. If he does not claim taking from the possessor's hand, it is not handed over to him because he has not proven the taking from his hand, as if someone claims a specific thing in the hand of a person that it is his property usurped from him, and the possessor brings evidence that it is a deposit with him for so-and-so, the claimant's evidence is accepted because he claims an act against him so he becomes a litigant; if he does not claim from his hand, his evidence is not accepted and he does not become a litigant. الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Satisfaction; taking possession as fulfillment of a right.

Liability for Denial of Trust Through Contradictory Statements
Complex ruling on liability for denial of trust

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of juhood al-amanah (denial of trust) to determine an agent's liability when his statements contradict regarding the possession of a trust property.

Core Idea
Contradictory statements from a trustee constitute denial of trust, making him liable for the property.

This lesson examines a case where an agent entrusted with pawning a gold coin gives conflicting statements about what he did. The Hanafi school uses this scenario to illustrate the principle that a trustee who first acknowledges then denies possession is considered to have denied the trust (juhood al-amanah) and becomes liable for the property's value. The ruling is built on qiyas to the case of a depositary who denies then admits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal relationship and the dispute
The principal gives a coin (value 20) to an agent to pawn for 10. The agent gives his own 10, says 'I pawned it', but the coin is destroyed. Later, the agent says 'I did not pawn it'.
2
Distinguish the two factual scenarios
If both agree the agent pawned, the agent is not liable and recovers his 10. If they dispute, the ruling depends on the agent's contradictory statements.
In the dispute scenario, the owner says 'you acknowledged pawning' and the agent denies.
3
Analyze the contradiction as denial of trust
Saying 'I pawned it' implies the coin left his possession (because pledge requires delivery). Saying 'I did not pawn it' implies it remained with him. This contradiction shows he first claimed he had no possession, then claimed he had possession – i.e., he denied the trust.
Juhood al-amanah is established by inconsistent statements about possession.
4
Apply the rule of juhood al-amanah
A trustee who denies the trust becomes liable for the value of the property. The principle is derived by qiyas from the depositary who says 'it is not with me' then 'it was with me'.
The agent becomes a guarantor (dhamin) for the coin's value.
5
Determine the final outcome
The principal can claim the value of the coin (20) from the agent, and the agent is entitled to recover his advance (10). Net effect: the principal recovers 10.
The objection of 'Isa that only the value should be owed is rejected because the agent's contradiction triggers juhood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دفع إلى آخر قلباً ليرهنه له عند رجل بعشرة ووزن القلب عشرون فأمسكه فأعطاه عشرة من عنده وقال رهنته ولم يقل رهنته عند آخر فهلك القلب، فإن تصادقا يرجع بالعشرة وكان أميناً في القلب وإن تجاحدا فقال أقررت بأنك رهنته فلا شيء له يقبل قوله بعد أن يحلف ما يعلم أنه أمسكه لأن الوكيل أقر أولاً أنه رهنه، فإذا قال لم أرهن فكأنه قال كذبت فيما أقررت به فأنكر المقر له فيكون القول للمقر له كما في سائر الأقارير فلا يرجع بالعشرة لأنه يثبت الرهن وقد هلك فصار الآمر موفياً العشرة بهلاك الرهن. وإنما يستحلف لأن المقر ادعى ما يحتمله إقراره لأنه يحتمل أنه لم يرهن غيره ورهنه من نفسه فلم يكن مناقضاً إلا أنه خلاف الظاهر، فإذا طلب يمين المقر له يستحلف كما لو أقر بالبيع ثم أصر. فإن قال الآمر للوكيل أقررت أنك رهنته ثم أقررت لم ترهنه فناقضت فأنت ضامن فله أن يضمنه قيمة القلب من الذهب ويضمن له العشرة؛ طعن عيسى وقال: الأوجه ضمان القيمة لأنهما لو تصادقا أنه لم يرهنه لا يضمن فكذلك إذا تصادقا أنه رهنه فإنه لا يضمن بالإرهان ولا يتركه. والجواب أنه يضمن بجحود الأمانة لأنه ثبت جحوده بالإقرارين لأنه لما قال رهنته فقد أقر أنه لم يكن في يده لأن الرهن لا يتم إلا بالتسليم، فلما قال لم أرهنه صار قائلاً أنه كان عندي وفي يدي وهذا هو معنى الجحود، ومن جحد أمانة في يده ضمنها وصار كالمودع إذا قال ليس عندي ثم قال كان عندي ضمن فكذا هذا.
He gave to another a gold coin to pawn it for him with a man for ten, while the weight of the coin was twenty, so he kept it and gave ten from himself and said 'I pawned it' and did not say 'I pawned it with another', then the coin was destroyed. If they agree, he recovers the ten and he was trustworthy regarding the coin. If they dispute and he [the owner] says 'you acknowledged that you pawned it', then there is nothing for him; his statement is accepted after he swears that he does not know that he kept it, because the agent first acknowledged that he pawned it. If he says 'I did not pawn it', it is as if he said 'you lied in what you acknowledged', and the acknowledgee denies, so the statement is of the acknowledgee as in other acknowledgments, so he does not recover the ten because the pledge is established and it has perished, so the principal becomes fulfilling the ten by the destruction of the pledge. He is only made to swear because the acknowledger claimed what his acknowledgment could bear, because it is possible that he did not pawn it to another but pawned it to himself, so it is not contradictory except that it is against the apparent. So if he requests the oath of the acknowledgee, he is sworn as if he acknowledged a sale then insisted. Then if the principal says to the agent: 'You acknowledged that you pawned it, then you acknowledged that you did not pawn it, so you contradicted, thus you are liable', then he may hold him liable for the value of the coin in gold and owe him the ten. Isa objected and said: the proper view is liability for the value because if they agree that he did not pawn it, he is not liable, so similarly if they agree that he pawned it, he is not liable by the pledge nor does he leave it. The answer: he is liable by denial of trust because his denial is established by the two acknowledgments: because when he said 'I pawned it', he acknowledged that it was not in his hand, since the pledge is not completed except by delivery; when he said 'I did not pawn it', he becomes saying that it was with me and in my hand, and this is the meaning of denial. Whoever denies a trust in his hand becomes liable for it, and it becomes like the depositary who says 'it is not with me' then says 'it was with me', he is liable. Similarly here.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage discusses a complex case where an agent receives a gold coin (qalb) to pawn for ten, but the coin is worth twenty (by weight). The agent keeps the coin, gives ten from himself, and says 'I pawned it' without specifying to another. The coin is then destroyed. If both agree, the agent recovers the ten he advanced and is not liable for the coin (he was a trustee). If they dispute: the owner says 'you acknowledged you pawned it' (so you owe me ten? or are liable?), the agent denies. The ruling: the agent's statement is accepted after an oath that he does not know he kept it, because the agent's initial acknowledgment ('I pawned it') is interpreted as pawning with the other person? Actually the reasoning is complex. The text says: the agent first acknowledged pawning; when he denies, it's like he is calling his own acknowledgment false, so the principal's (owner's) statement is taken, and the agent does not recover the ten because the pledge is established and destroyed, so the principal is deemed to have paid the ten via destruction? Then, if the principal directly says to the agent: 'You first acknowledged pawning then denied, so you contradicted, thus you are liable for the value of the coin,' the principal can claim the value (twenty) from the agent and must also give the agent the ten? The objection of 'Isa (possibly Isa ibn Aban, a Hanafi scholar): the proper view is only liability for the value (twenty) because if they agree he didn't pawn, he's not liable; if they agree he did pawn, he's not liable for the pledge. The Hanafi response: he is liable because his contradiction amounts to a denial of trust (juhood al-amanah). By saying 'I pawned it', he claimed the coin left his possession (as delivery is required for pledge); by saying 'I did not pawn it', he claims it remained in his possession. This inconsistency means he is a trustee who first denied then admitted, so he is liable, similar to a depositary who denies then admits taking the deposit.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): A gold coin; specifically a dinar or a coin of known weight (here weight 20).
جحود الأمانة (juhood al-amanah): Denial of a trust; when a trustee denies possession of the trust property, he becomes liable for it.
الوكيل (al-wakeel): Agent; the person entrusted with pawning the coin on behalf of the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of the gold coin, why is the agent liable for the value of the coin even though he was a trustee?
A) Because he lost the coin through negligence.
B) Because his contradictory statements constitute a denial of trust.
C) Because he advanced his own money without authorization.
D) Because the pledge was void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
A trustee who denies the trust through contradictory statements becomes a guarantor for the property's value, even if the underlying facts would not otherwise create liability.

The Mortgagee's Right to Demand Debt and Imprison
Ruling on mortgagee's right to demand and imprison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the mortgagee may demand the debt and imprison the mortgagor, and explain the rationale that the pledge is additional security.

Core Idea
Holding the pledge does not waive the mortgagee's right to demand payment; the pledge is security, not payment.

A mortgagee who holds a pledge might wonder whether he can still demand the debt from the mortgagor or even have him imprisoned for procrastination. The Hanafi school clarifies that the pledge is merely additional security and does not forfeit the mortgagee's substantive right. This lesson explores the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act under discussion is the mortgagee demanding his debt and imprisoning the mortgagor. The ruling is that this is permissible and valid (sahih).
Ruling is permissive, not obligatory.
2
Locate the proof (talil)
The commentary provides the reasoning: the mortgagee's right to the debt remains, and the pledge is only for additional security (ziyadat al-siyanah). Imprisonment is a penalty for procrastination (mumatalah), which is injustice.
This is a rational proof, not a textual one.
3
Note the internal Hanafi support
Imam al-Karkhi in his Mukhtasar explicitly affirms this ruling, stating that neither the pledging nor the possession of the pledge prevents demand.
Al-Karkhi's view is relied upon.
4
Identify the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may not allow imprisonment for debt, viewing it as excessive. The Hanafi position is that it is a legitimate penalty.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القضاء يمنع. قال رحمه الله: (وله أن يطالب الراهن بدينه ويحبسه) به أي للمرتهن أن يطالب الراهن بدينه وبحبسه به وإن كان الرهن في يده لأن حقه باق والرهن لزيادة الصيانة فلا تمتنع المطالبة، وكذا لا يمتنع الحبس به لأنه جزاء الظلم وهو المماطلة على ما بيناه مفصلاً. وقال الكرخي في مختصره: وللمرتهن مطالبة الراهن بدينه إذا كان مالاً ولا يمنعه الارتهان به من ذلك ولا كون الرهن في يده، وكذلك إذا كان مؤجلاً وحل فإنه لا حبسه؛ كذا في العيني على الهداية. قال رحمه الله: (ويؤمر المرتهن بإحضار رهنه والراهن بإداء دينه) أو لا أي إذا طلب المرتهن دينه يؤمر بإحضار الرهن أولاً ليعلم أنه باق ولأنه قبض الرهن قبل الاستيفاء، ولا يجوز أن يقبض ما له مع قيام يد الاستيفاء لأنه يؤدي إلى تكرار الاستيفاء على اعتبار الهلاك في يد المرتهن وهو يحتمل. ولو قال بإحضار رهنه لو في يده لكان أولى ليخرج ما إذا كان في يد عدل فإنه لا يؤمر بإحضاره كما سنبين. وإذا أحضر المرتهن الرهن أمر الراهن بتسليم الدين أولاً وهو المراد بقوله والراهن بإداء دينه أولاً ليتعين حق المرتهن في الدين كما تعين حق الراهن في الرهن تحقيقاً للتسوية بينهما كما في تسليم المبيع والثمن يحضر البائع المبيع ثم يسلم المشتري الثمن أولاً لما ذكرنا. وإن طالبه بالدين في غير البلد الذي وقع العقد فيه فإن كان الرهن لا حمل له ولا مؤنة فكذلك الجواب لأن الأماكن كلها في حقه كبقعة واحدة في حق التسليم ولهذا لا يشترط فيه بيان مكان الإيفاء في باب السلم بالإجماع، وإن كان له حمل ومؤنة فيستوفي دينه ولا يكلف إحضار الرهن لأن الواجب عليه التسليم بالتخلية دون النقل لأنه يتضرر به زيادة ضرر لم تلزمه في العقد. ولو باع الرهن لا يكلف المشتري إحضار الرهن لأنه لا قدرة له عليه لأن بيعه بأمر الراهن صحيح وصار الرهن ديناً فصار كأنه رهنه الراهن وهو دين. ولو قبض الثمن يكلف إحضاره لقيام البدل مقام المبدل والذي يقبض الثمن هو البائع، مرتهناً كان أو عدلاً،
The court prevents. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he may demand the mortgagor for his debt and imprison him) meaning the mortgagee may demand the mortgagor for his debt and imprison him thereby even if the pledge is in his hand, because his right remains and the pledge is for additional security, so the demand is not prevented. Likewise, imprisonment is not prevented because it is the penalty for injustice, which is procrastination, as explained in detail. Al-Karkhi said in his Mukhtasar: The mortgagee may demand the mortgagor for his debt if it is property, and neither the pledging nor the pledge being in his hand prevents that. Likewise if it is deferred and becomes due, he may imprison him; so in al-Ayni on al-Hidayah. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the mortgagee is ordered to produce his pledge and the mortgagor to pay his debt) meaning if the mortgagee demands his debt, he is ordered to produce the pledge first to know that it remains, and because he seized the pledge before satisfaction, and it is not permissible for him to take what is his while the hand of satisfaction exists because it leads to repetition of satisfaction based on destruction in the mortgagee's hand, and that is possible. And if he said 'produce his pledge' if it is in his hand, it would be better to exclude the case when it is with a third party, for then he is not ordered to produce it as we will explain. When the mortgagee produces the pledge, the mortgagor is ordered to pay the debt first, which is meant by his words 'and the mortgagor to pay his debt first', so that the mortgagee's right in the debt becomes specific just as the mortgagor's right in the pledge becomes specific, achieving equality between them, like in delivery of sale and price: the seller produces the goods then the buyer pays the price first for the reasons mentioned. If he demands the debt in a town other than where the contract took place, if the pledge has no carrying cost or expense, the answer is the same because all places are like one spot for delivery, and for this reason specifying the place of payment is not required in salam by consensus. If it has carrying cost and expense, he collects his debt and is not required to produce the pledge because the obligation on him is delivery by vacating not by transport, as that would cause him extra harm not obligated in the contract. If he sold the pledge, the buyer is not required to produce the pledge because he has no power over it, since the sale by order of the mortgagor is valid and the pledge becomes a debt, so it is as if the mortgagor pawned it while it is a debt. If he received the price, he is required to produce it because the substitute stands in place of the substituted, and the one who receives the price is the seller, whether he is the mortgagee or a trustee.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage deals with the mortgagee's procedural rights. First, the mortgagee may both demand the debt from the mortgagor and imprison him for non-payment, even though the pledge is already in his possession. The reason: the debt remains due, and the pledge is merely additional security. Imprisonment is a penalty for procrastination. This is supported by the view of Imam al-Karkhi. Second, when the mortgagee demands payment, he must first produce the pledge (if it is in his hand) to prove it still exists and to avoid double recovery. The judge then orders the mortgagor to pay the debt. This ensures that both parties' rights are secured: the mortgagee shows the pledge, and the mortgagor pays. If the demand is made in a different city, the mortgagee is not required to transport the pledge if that would be burdensome; he can simply demand payment without producing the pledge. However, if the pledge is easily transportable, he must produce it. If the mortgagee sells the pledge (with the mortgagor's permission), the buyer is not required to produce the pledge because he is not the one who seized it originally; but if the mortgagee receives the sale price, he must produce the amount received as it stands in place of the pledge.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment by the court as a penalty for procrastination in debt payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of holding a pledge on the mortgagee's right to demand the debt?
A) It invalidates the right because the debt is considered satisfied.
B) It does not prevent the demand because the pledge is additional security.
C) It only allows demand if the pledge is returned first.
D) It converts the debt into a sale.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's right to demand payment and imprison for procrastination is not negated by possession of the pledge.

Procedure for Producing the Pledge and Paying the Debt
Procedure for producing pledge and paying debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence demanded by the court when the mortgagee seeks payment: the mortgagee must first produce the pledge, then the mortgagor pays, with exceptions for different towns and sold pledges.

Core Idea
The mortgagee must first prove the pledge exists; only then is the mortgagor ordered to pay, ensuring fairness.

When a mortgagee exercises his right to demand payment, the court follows a specific procedure to protect both parties. The mortgagee must first produce the pledge (if in his possession) to verify its existence and avoid double recovery. Only then is the mortgagor ordered to pay. This lesson explains the order, its rationale, and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default order
When the mortgagee demands payment, the judge first orders him to produce the pledge. Once produced, the mortgagor is ordered to pay the debt.
This order is analogous to sale: seller produces goods, buyer pays.
2
Identify the rationale
The mortgagee must produce the pledge to verify it still exists and to prevent potential double satisfaction (if the pledge is destroyed, the mortgagee might claim both the pledge and the debt).
The text says 'to know that it remains' and to avoid repetition of satisfaction.
3
Note exceptions when the pledge is in a different town
If the pledge is in a different town and has significant carrying cost, the mortgagee is not required to produce it; he can simply collect his debt. If transport is easy, he must produce it.
The principle: delivery is by takhliyah (vacating) not physical transport if burdensome.
4
Handle the case when the pledge has been sold
If the mortgagee sold the pledge (with permission), the buyer is not required to produce it because the buyer did not seize it. However, if the mortgagee receives the price, he must produce the money.
The substitute (price) stands in place of the pledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

التخلية (at-takhliyah): Vacating possession; not required to physically transport the pledge to the mortgagee.

Guarantee of Agent Who Contradicts Himself About the Pledge
Ruling on an agent's liability when he first affirms then denies pledging property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an agent who contradicts himself about pledging property becomes liable in the Hanafi school, and evaluate the opposing view of 'Isa ibn Aban using qiyas.

Core Idea
Contradiction in acknowledging a trust constitutes denial (جحود), making the agent liable by analogy to the depositee.

When an agent first affirms then denies that he pledged a property, his contradiction raises a question of trust. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that such contradiction makes him liable (ضامن) due to denial of trust (جحود الأمانة), and contrasts it with the view of 'Isa ibn Aban who argued for consistency. Understanding the basis of liability is crucial for agency and pledge contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradictory statements
The agent first says 'I pledged it' (implying not in his possession) then says 'I did not pledge it' (implying it was in his possession). This contradiction is the key fact.
2
Understand the principle of denial of trust (جحود الأمانة)
In Hanafi fiqh, denying a trust that was in one's possession triggers liability. The contradiction here establishes denial because the second statement contradicts the first, revealing that the item was in his possession.
3
Apply qiyas to the depositee case
The text analogizes to a depositee (مودع) who first denies then admits the deposit. Such a depositee becomes liable. Similarly, the agent's contradiction constitutes denial, making him liable.
The illa (effective cause) is the denial of trust.
4
Analyze 'Isa ibn Aban's objection
'Isa argues that consistency should be considered: if both agree no pledge, no liability; if both agree pledge, no liability for the act. The Hanafi response is that liability arises from the contradiction itself, not from the existence of the pledge.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the agent is liable. This is supported by qiyas on the depositee, which establishes liability for denial of trust.
The tarjih authority is the text's author, who rejects 'Isa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان أنك قال كان تلجئة أو كان فيه خيار شرط، فإن قال الآمر للوكيل أقررت أنك رهنته ثم أقررت لم ترهنه فناقضت فأنت ضامن فله أن يضمنه قيمة القلب من الذهب ويضمن له العشرة؛ طعن عيسى وقال : الأوجه ضمان القيمة لأنهما لو تصادقا أنه لم يرهنه لا يضمن فكذلك إذا تصادقا أنه رهنه فإنه لا يضمن بالإرهان ولا يتركه والجواب أنه يضمن بجحود الأمانة لأنه ثبت جحوده بالإقرارين لأنه لما قال رهنته فقد أقر أنه لم يكن في يده لأن الرهن لا يتم إلا بالتسليم، فلما قال لم أرهنه صار قائلاً أنه كان عندي وفي يدي وهذا هو معنى الجحود هو معنى الجحود ومن جحد أمانة في يده ضمنها وصار كالمودع إذا قال ليس عندي ثم قال كان عندي ضمن فكذا هذا.
If it is a collusive pledge or there is an option of condition, then if the principal said to the agent: 'You have acknowledged that you pledged it, then you acknowledged that you did not pledge it, so you contradicted, so you are guarantor.' So he can make him liable for the value of the heart of gold and guarantee him the ten. 'Isa objected and said: The more appropriate is guarantee of value because if they both acknowledge that he did not pledge it, he is not liable, so likewise if they both acknowledge that he pledged it, he is not liable for pledging and should not be left. The answer is that he is liable because of denial of trust, because his denial is established by the two acknowledgements: when he said 'I pledged it' he acknowledged that it was not in his possession because a pledge is not completed except by delivery, and when he said 'I did not pledge it' he became saying that it was with me and in my hand, and this is the meaning of denial. Whoever denies a trust in his hand becomes liable for it, and it is like the depositee: if he says 'it is not with me' then says 'it was with me', he is liable. Similarly this case.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage discusses a case of collusive pledge (تلجئة) or pledge with option (خيار شرط). The principal tells the agent: you first said you pledged, then you said you didn't – this contradiction makes you liable. The ruling gives the principal the option to demand guarantee of the value (قيمة القلب من الذهب) and also guarantee of the ten (العشرة). Scholar 'Isa ibn Aban objects, stating the more appropriate ruling is guarantee of value. He argues that if both parties agree that no pledge occurred, the agent is not liable; similarly if they agree that a pledge did occur, the agent is not liable for the act of pledging itself. The text's response is that the liability arises from denial of trust (جحود الأمانة), not from the pledging act. By first saying 'I pledged', the agent admitted the item was not in his possession (since pledge requires delivery). By then saying 'I did not pledge', he effectively claims it was in his possession – this contradiction constitutes a denial of the trust. The analogy is drawn from the depositee (مودع): if he first denies the deposit and later admits, he is liable for the value. Thus, the agent is liable.

Key Terms
تلجئة (talji'ah): A collusive pledge where the transaction is a sham to conceal a debt.
خيار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in the contract allowing a party to cancel within a specified period.
جحود الأمانة (juhud al-amanah): Denial that something held in trust was ever in one's possession, leading to liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the agent become liable (ضامن) when he first says 'I pledged' then says 'I did not pledge'?
A) Because he admitted to pledging, which requires delivery, then denied it, thus denying the trust.
B) Because pledging without permission makes him liable.
C) Because he caused the principal to lose the gold.
D) Because he contradicted himself, which nullifies the agency.

Key Takeaway
The agent who contradicts himself about a pledge becomes liable because the contradiction constitutes denial of trust (جحود الأمانة), by analogy to the depositee.

Creditor's Right to Demand and Imprison Despite Pledge
Ruling that a mortgagee may demand payment and imprison the mortgagor even while holding the pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mortgagee's right to demand payment and imprison the debtor, and explain the underlying reasoning (talil).

Core Idea
Pledge possession does not extinguish the debt; the creditor's rights remain intact.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a common misconception in the law of pledge (rahn). Many assume that once the creditor takes possession of the pledge, he can no longer demand the debt or seek imprisonment. The Hanafi school, however, firmly holds that the pledge is only an additional security, leaving the creditor's original rights fully intact. We will unpack the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, extract the exact ruling: the mortgagee may demand payment and imprison the mortgagor even though the pledge is already in his hand.
2
Examine the reasoning (talil)
Next, analyze the justification: the right to the debt remains; the pledge is for additional security only; imprisonment is a penalty for procrastination (mumatalah).
3
Locate the supporting evidence
Note the citation of al-Karkhi’s Mukhtasar, which confirms the ruling and extends it to due deferred debts. Understand that this is a reasoning-based proof, not an explicit scriptural text.
4
Understand the practical effect
Finally, see how this ruling applies: the creditor can pursue both remedies—holding the pledge and demanding payment/imprisoning—simultaneously.
Imprisonment is contingent on procrastination, not mere inability to pay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وله أن يطالب الراهن بدينه ويحبسه (به أي للمرتهن أن يطالب الراهن بدينه وبحبسه به وإن كان بعد الرهن في يده لأن حقه باق والرهن لزيادة الصيانة فلا تمتنع المطالبة، وكذا لا يمتنع الحبس به لأنه جزاء الظلم وهو المماطلة على ما بيناه في مفصلاً. وقال الكرخي في مختصره وللمرتهن مطالبة الراهن بدينه إذا كان مالاً ولا يمنعه الارتهان به من ذلك ولا كون الرهن في يده، وكذلك إذا كان مؤجلاً وحل فإنه لا . حبسه ؛ كذا في العيني على الهداية
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And he has the right to demand the debt from the pledgor and to imprison him for it) meaning that the mortgagee may demand the debt from the pledgor and imprison him for it even if the pledge is already in his hand, because his right remains and the pledge is for additional security, so demand is not prevented. Likewise, imprisonment for it is not prevented because it is a penalty for wrongdoing, which is procrastination, as we have detailed elsewhere. And al-Karkhi said in his Mukhtasar: The mortgagee may demand the debt from the pledgor if it is property, and pledging does not prevent that, nor does the pledge being in his hand. Also if it is deferred and becomes due, then he may imprison him. As is in al-Ayni on al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the creditor (مرتهن) retains the right to demand payment of the debt and to have the debtor (راهن) imprisoned even though the pledge is already in his possession. The reason is that his right to the debt is not satisfied by mere possession of the pledge; the pledge is only to secure the debt. Imprisonment is justified as a penalty for delaying payment (مماطلة). Al-Karkhi in his Mukhtasar confirms this ruling: the creditor may demand the debt, and the existence of the pledge or its possession does not prevent that. The same applies if the debt is deferred and becomes due – the creditor may then imprison the debtor. The commentary references al-Ayni's work on al-Hidayah for further details. This ruling emphasizes that the pledge does not eliminate the debtor's obligation; it merely secures it.

Key Terms
المطالبة (al-mutalabah): Demanding the debt from the debtor.
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment to coerce payment, as a penalty for procrastination.
المماطلة (al-mumatalah): Procrastination or unjustifiable delay in paying the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the mortgagee may demand payment and imprison the mortgagor despite holding the pledge?
A) Because the pledge is in the mortgagee's hand, he has full control.
B) Because the debt remains and the pledge is only for additional security.
C) Because the mortgagor has committed a crime.
D) Because the pledge is not valid without a court order.

Key Takeaway
The creditor's right to demand payment and imprison the debtor persists even when the pledge is in his possession, as the pledge is merely a security, not a satisfaction of the debt.
